Biography of Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani (Abu Hanifa al-Asghar)
Biographical entry for a Hanafi scholar known as 'the younger Abu Hanifa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, nisbah, and title of Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, and explain the significance of the title 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar' in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani was called 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar' because of his mastery in Hanafi fiqh, reflecting the high esteem for his scholarship.

This lesson introduces a key figure in the Hanafi school: Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani. Though his name may not be as familiar as later scholars, his title 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar' – the younger Abu Hanifa – speaks volumes about his rank. Understanding his background helps us appreciate the chain of transmission of Hanafi fiqh and the scholarly network of the 4th century AH.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name
The text gives his full name and nisbah: Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Faqih al-Balkhi al-Hindawani. Write it down with the Arabic.
The nisbah 'al-Balkhi' indicates he was from Balkh, 'al-Hindawani' from the locality Hindawan.
2
Understand the title 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar'
The title is a great honor, comparing him to Imam Abu Hanifa. Why was he given this title? Because he was baran (brilliant) in fiqh and the leading scholar of his time.
This shows that later Hanafi scholars were recognized for their mastery.
3
Note his death year and location
He died in Bukhara in 362 AH. This places him in the 4th century AH, a key period for the compilation of Hanafi texts.
Bukhara was a major center of Islamic learning.
4
Locate Hindawan
Hindawan is a locality in Balkh. This geographical detail helps trace scholarly origins.
Balkh is in present-day Afghanistan.
5
Recognize the source
The entry is from Imam al-Yafi'i, a later biographer, indicating the transmission of this information.
Knowing sources is important for evaluating riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۳ - أبو جعفر الهندواني : هو أبو جعفر محمد بن عبد الله الفقيه البلخی الهندواني، كان بارعاً في الفقه، شيخ زمانه يقال له : أبو حنيفة الأصغر . توفى ببخارى سنة اثنتين وستين وثلاثمائة . كذا قال الإمام اليافعي . و الهندوان" (بفتح الدات وكسر الهاء) محلة ببلخ .
13- Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani: He is Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Faqih al-Balkhi al-Hindawani. He was brilliant in fiqh, the shaykh of his time, called 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar' (the younger Abu Hanifa). He died in Bukhara in the year 362 AH. Thus said Imam al-Yafi'i. And 'al-Hindawan' (with a fatha on the dal and kasra on the ha) is a locality in Balkh.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This is a short biographical entry for Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, a Hanafi jurist from Balkh. He was known as 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar' due to his expertise in fiqh. The entry gives his death year as 362 AH and notes that 'al-Hindawan' is a locality in Balkh (present-day Afghanistan).

Key Terms
أبو حنيفة الأصغر (Abu Hanifa al-Asghar): A title given to al-Hindawani, meaning 'the younger Abu Hanifa', indicating his mastery of Hanafi fiqh.
الهندواني (al-Hindawani): A nisbah referring to a place called Hindawan in Balkh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To which locality does the nisbah 'al-Hindawani' refer?
A) A district in Baghdad
B) A locality in Balkh
C) A village near Bukhara
D) A region in India

Key Takeaway
Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani was a leading Hanafi jurist of the 4th century AH, honored with the title 'Abu Hanifa al-Asghar', reflecting his mastery of fiqh and his high standing in the school.

Biography of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and His Ijtihad Rank
Biographical entry for a Hanafi mujtahid from Karkh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and explain his rank as a mujtahid fi al-masa'il within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi was a Hanafi jurist classified as a mujtahid fi al-masa'il, a rank below absolute ijtihad but crucial for deriving cases within the school.

This passage introduces us to Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, a prominent Hanafi scholar from the 3rd/9th-4th/10th century. His classification by Ibn al-Kamal as a mujtahid fi al-masa'il tells us about the hierarchical structure of Hanafi ijtihad and the role of such scholars in the school's development.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's name and nisbah
Read the full name and the nisbah (relative attribution) to Karkh. Note how the name is structured: Ubaydullah ibn al-Husayn, Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi.
Nisbah often indicates geographic origin.
2
Extract birth and death dates
Note the Hijri years: born 260 AH, died 340 AH on the night of mid-Sha'ban. This places him in the late 3rd to mid-4th century AH.
These dates help contextualize his scholarly contributions.
3
Identify the source of classification and the rank
The text says Ibn al-Kamal mentioned him among 'the class of mujtahidin fi al-masa'il'. This is a specific rank in Hanafi ijtihad hierarchy.
Ibn al-Kamal is a later Hanafi biographer and jurist.
4
Understand the term mujtahid fi al-masa'il
This rank means the scholar is capable of deriving rulings for new cases (masa'il) within the school's established principles, but not at the level of absolute ijtihad.
It is distinct from mujtahid fi al-madhhab and mujtahid mutlaq.
5
Note the incomplete nature of the entry
The text ends abruptly with 'وكذا عده', suggesting the biography may continue in the source. Recognize that some historical records are fragmentary.
Iftaa training often requires working with incomplete sources.

Source Text

١٤ - أبو الحسن الكرخى : هو عبيد الله بن الحسين أبو الحسن الكرخي : نسبة إلى "كرخ " ( وهى قرية بنواحي العراق) كان مولده سنة ٢٦٠هـ، ومات سنة ٣٤٠هـ ليلة النصف من شعبان وقد ذكره ابن الكمال من طبقة المجتهدين في المسائل، وكذا عده
14- Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi: He is Ubaydullah ibn al-Husayn Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, relative to 'Karkh' (a village in the region of Iraq). He was born in 260 AH and died in 340 AH on the night of the middle of Sha'ban. Ibn al-Kamal mentioned him among the class of mujtahidin fi al-masa'il, and likewise counted him.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, a Hanafi jurist from Karkh (near Baghdad). He was born in 260 AH and died in 340 AH. The entry notes that Ibn al-Kamal classified him as a mujtahid fi al-masa'il, a rank of ijtihad within the Hanafi school. The text appears to be cut off at the end of the page.

Key Terms
المجتهدين في المسائل (al-mujtahidin fi al-masa'il): A rank of ijtihad in which the scholar deduces rulings for new cases within the school's principles.
كرخ (Karkh): A village near Baghdad, the place of origin of al-Karkhi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mujtahid mutlaq
B) Mujtahid fi al-madhhab
C) Mujtahid fi al-masa'il
D) Mujtahid fi al-usul

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi was a Hanafi mujtahid fi al-masa'il, a crucial rank for deriving rulings within the school's framework.

The Life and Rank of Imam al-Quduri
Biography of al-Quduri with rank debate and miracle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the biographical details of al-Quduri and explain the debate about his rank in the Hanafi hierarchy of mujtahids.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's rank is debated: was he an as-hab al-tarjih or higher? His Mukhtasar's miraculous correction shows his spiritual stature.

Imam al-Quduri is one of the most famous Hanafi jurists, author of the foundational Mukhtasar al-Quduri. But where does he stand in the Hanafi mujtahid hierarchy? This lesson explores his biography, the controversy over his rank, and a remarkable story that underscores his connection with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the biographical facts
Extract from the passage: full name, dates of birth and death, burial details, and the two theories about his nisba.
Pay attention to the precision of dates and the two possible origins of 'al-Quduri'.
2
Understand the rank classification
Learn the term 'as-hab al-tarjih' and its meaning in the Hanafi hierarchy: those who can prefer between narrations but cannot perform ijtihad.
Compare this to higher ranks like as-hab al-takhrij or absolute mujtahid.
3
Analyze the rank controversy
Note that Ibn Kamal Pasha placed al-Quduri among as-hab al-tarjih, but a later scholar objected because al-Quduri was earlier and more knowledgeable than al-Halwani, who was ranked higher.
Consider why chronological precedence and breadth of knowledge might affect ranking.
4
Reflect on the miraculous story
The story from al-Ayni: after completing the Mukhtasar, al-Quduri prayed during Hajj for Allah to show him any errors, and found five or six places erased.
This is considered a karamah (miracle) and indicates divine acceptance of his work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٥ - أبو الحسين القدورى : هو أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد أبو الحسين البغدادى القدوري (بالضم) قيل : إنه نسبة إلى قرية من قرى بغداد يقال له : "قدورة". وقيل : نسبة إلى بيع "القدر" . وكانت ولادته كما في الأنساب) سنة ٣٦٢هـ. ووفاته (كما فى وفيات الأعيان يوم الأحد، الخامس من رجب سنة ٤٢٨هـ. ودفن من يومه بداره في درب أبي خلف ثم نقل إلى تربة في شارع المنصور ودفن هناك بجنب أبي بكر الخوارزمي الحنفى ذكره ابن كمال الرومي ومن تبعه في أصحاب الترجيح من المقلدين الذين شأنهم تفضيل بعض الروايات على بعض من دون قدرة على الاجتهاد، وتعقبه بعض الفضلاء : بأن القدورى متقدم على شمس الأئمة الحلوانى زمانًا، وأعلى منه كعباً، وأطول باعا، فما باله نقص مرتبته عن مرتبته؟ والله أعلم .
عجيبة : ذكر العيني في شرح الهداية : " أن القدورى لما فرغ من تصنيف مختصره المنسوب إليه، حج، وأخذ المختصر معه، ولما فرغ من طوافه سأل الله سبحانه أن يوقفه على خطأ فيه وسهو منه عن قلم، ثم إنه فتح المختصر وتصفحه ورقة ورقة إلى آخره فوجد فيه خمسة مواضع أو ستة مواضع ممحوة. وهذا يعد من كرامته " .
15 - Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri: He is Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad, Abu al-Husayn al-Baghdadi al-Quduri (with damm on qaf). It is said that this is a relative to a village of Baghdad called 'Qadura'. And it is said: relative to selling 'qudur' (pots). His birth was as in al-Ansab in the year 362 AH. His death (as in Wafayat al-Ayan) on Sunday, the 5th of Rajab 428 AH. He was buried on that day in his house in Darb Abi Khalaf, then moved to a burial ground in the street of al-Mansur and buried there next to Abu Bakr al-Khwarizmi al-Hanafi. Ibn Kamal al-Rumi and those who followed him mentioned him among the 'as-hab al-tarjih' of the muqallidin, whose job is to prefer some narrations over others without ability to perform ijtihad. And some virtuous person objected to that: because al-Quduri preceded Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani in time, and is higher than him in status, and more extensive in knowledge, so how can his rank be lower than his? And Allah knows best.
A wonder: al-Ayni mentioned in Sharh al-Hidayah: 'When al-Quduri finished writing his Mukhtasar attributed to him, he performed Hajj and took the Mukhtasar with him. When he finished his tawaf, he asked Allah the Exalted to show him a mistake or an oversight from his pen. Then he opened the Mukhtasar and flipped through it leaf by leaf to its end, and found five or six places that had been erased. This is considered one of his miracles.'
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This is a detailed biography of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the famous Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It gives his full name, his nisba, two theories about its origin, his birth and death dates, and burial details. Importantly, it discusses his rank in the Hanafi hierarchy: Ibn Kamal Pasha placed him among the 'as-hab al-tarjih' (those who can give preference among narrations but cannot perform ijtihad). However, a later scholar objected, noting that al-Quduri was earlier and more knowledgeable than al-Halwani (who was considered a higher rank), so it is incongruous to rank him lower. The passage ends with a miraculous story from al-Ayni about how Allah answered his prayer to correct errors in his Mukhtasar after completing it.

Key Terms
أصحاب الترجيح (as-hab al-tarjih): Those who can prefer one narration over another but cannot perform ijtihad; a rank in the Hanafi hierarchy.
مقلدون (muqallidun): Jurists who follow the madhhab without ijtihad; but can still prefer rulings within the school.
كرامة (karamah): A miracle granted to a saint (wali) as a sign of divine favor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What miraculous event is attributed to al-Quduri regarding his Mukhtasar?
A) It was written in one night
B) Errors were erased after prayer during Hajj
C) It was praised by the Prophet in a dream
D) It was found unchanged for centuries

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's biography highlights the importance of understanding scholarly hierarchies within the Hanafi school, and his miraculous story underscores the spiritual dimension of fiqh work.

Abu Hafs al-Bukhari: The Senior Student of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Biography with a textual correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Abu Hafs al-Kabir's place in the Hanafi chain of transmission and correct a common textual error regarding his son's name.

Core Idea
Abu Hafs al-Kabir was the foremost Hanafi scholar in Bukhara and a direct student of Muhammad al-Shaybani.

This biography introduces Abu Hafs al-Bukhari, a key link in the Hanafi chain of transmission. Understanding his role as the head of the Hanafi scholars in Bukhara and his student relationship with Imam Muhammad helps us appreciate the spread of the Hanafi school in Central Asia. The passage also demonstrates the importance of manuscript criticism in preserving accurate biographical records.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and his title
Abu Hafs al-Bukhari is called 'al-Kabir' to distinguish him from his son. Note his kunya and nisba.
The title 'al-Kabir' indicates seniority.
2
Trace his teachers
He studied fiqh from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (al-Shaybani) and Shams al-A'imma.
Muhammad al-Shaybani is a founder of the Hanafi school.
3
Recognise his students and influence
He became the head (riyasa) of the Hanafi scholars in Bukhara and had many followers.
This shows his authority in the region.
4
Note the textual correction
The passage corrects a common error: his son's name is Hafs, not Ja'far.
Tashif (distortion) is a known issue in manuscripts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٦ - أبو حفص البخارى : هو أبو حفص الكبير، أخذ الفقه عن محمد ابن الحسن وعن شمس الأئمة وتوصيفه بـ "الكبير" بالنسبة إلى ابنه فإنه يكنى بأبي حفص الصغير، وكان رحمه الله من كبار تلامذة محمد بن الحسن . انتهت إليه رياسة الأصحاب ببخارى توفّى سنة ٢١٧هـ . وله أصحاب وأتباع كثيرون . واسم ابنه " حفص"، كما في مقدمة الهداية والفوائد والجواهر المضيئة. وما في كتاب الكنى من الجواهر المضيئة أن اسمه "جعفر" فهو تصحيف .
16 - Abu Hafs al-Bukhari: He is Abu Hafs al-Kabir. He studied fiqh from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and from Shams al-A'imma. And he is described as 'al-Kabir' in relation to his son, for he is called Abu Hafs al-Saghir. He, may Allah have mercy on him, was among the senior students of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. The leadership of the companions in Bukhara ended with him. He died in 217 AH. He had many companions and followers. The name of his son is 'Hafs', as in the introduction of al-Hidayah, al-Fawa'id, and al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah. And what is in the book al-Kuna from al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah that his name is 'Ja'far' is a distortion.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This entry gives the biography of Abu Hafs al-Kabir, a prominent Hanafi scholar of Bukhara. He was a direct student of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and also studied with Shams al-A'imma (probably al-Halwani). The title 'al-Kabir' distinguishes him from his son, also called Abu Hafs (al-Saghir). He became the head of the Hanafi school in Bukhara. The passage also clarifies the name of his son: it is Hafs, not Ja'far, correcting a common mistake.

Key Terms
رياسة الأصحاب (riyasat al-as-hab): Leadership/headship of the Hanafi scholars in a region.
تصحيف (tashif): Distortion or misreading of a word in a manuscript.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa
B) Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani
C) Abu Yusuf
D) Al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
Abu Hafs al-Kabir was a senior student of Muhammad al-Shaybani and the head of Hanafi scholars in Bukhara; his son's name is Hafs, not Ja'far.

Biography of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani
Biography of a Hanafi scholar and transmitter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the works of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani and state his significance in the Hanafi transmission chain.

Core Idea
Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani authored foundational Hanafi texts and refused the judiciary, cementing his legacy as a transmitter of the school.

This lesson introduces Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, a key student of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. His writings, such as al-Mabsut and al-Siyar al-Saghir, are essential sources of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding his role helps you grasp how the Hanafi school preserved its rulings.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the name and teacher
The text states he studied fiqh from Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan). This places him in the immediate chain after the founder.
His kunya is Abu Sulayman.
2
Recall his authored works
He wrote several books that became part of Zahir al-Riwayah. The text lists al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Nawadir, al-Mabsut, as well as Masail al-Usul and al-Amali.
Al-Mabsut is the original; later Sarakhsi expanded it.
3
Remember his rejection of judiciary
Al-Ma'mun offered him qada, but he refused, indicating his piety and dedication to teaching.
This is a common trait among early Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٧- أبو سليمان الجوزجاني : هو موسى بن سليمان، أبو سليمان الجوزجاني ، أخذ الفقه عن محمد، وكتب مسائل الأصول والأمالي، وكان مشاركًا المعلى ابن منصور عرض عليه المأمون القضاء فلم يقبل . توفى بعد المائتين. وله السير الصغير والنوادر والمبسوط وغير ذلك .
17 - Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani: He is Musa ibn Sulayman, Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani. He studied fiqh from Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan). He wrote the Masail al-Usul and al-Amali. He was a participant [in discussion?] with al-Mu'alla ibn Mansur. Al-Ma'mun offered him the judiciary but he did not accept. He died after 200 AH. He authored al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Nawadir, al-Mabsut, and others.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This is a short biography of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, another student of Imam Muhammad. He wrote important early Hanafi texts: al-Siyar al-Saghir (on siyar), al-Nawadir (rare transmissions), and al-Mabsut (the original mabsut, which later scholars like al-Sarakhsi expanded). He was offered the position of qadi by the caliph al-Ma'mun but refused, showing his piety and disinterest in worldly authority.

Key Terms
الأمالي (al-amali): Dictations or sessions where a scholar dictated hadith/fiqh to students.
السير الصغير (al-siyar al-saghir): A book by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan on sirah and jihad; al-Juzjani transmitted it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Governor of Basra
B) Chief mufti
C) Qadi (judge)
D) Imam of the mosque

Key Takeaway
Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani was a key transmitter of Hanafi fiqh whose works remain authoritative.

Distinguishing Two Abu al-Layths: The Faqih and the Hafiz
Biographical clarification of two scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two scholars named Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi and distinguish them based on their titles, death dates, and works.

Core Idea
Two scholars named Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi existed: the earlier Hafiz and the later Faqih.

This passage from Uqud Rasm al-Mufti introduces a key challenge in Hanafi biography: multiple scholars share the same name. Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi is a major figure, but as the text shows, there were actually two distinct scholars with that name—one a hadith specialist (al-Hafiz) and the other a jurist (al-Faqih). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly attributing fatwa works like al-Nawazil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject's full name and title
Read the first line: the scholar is Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim, known as 'Imam al-Huda'. Note that his death date is disputed in later sources.
The text gives a chain of transmission but the focus is on the confusion over his death year.
2
Analyze the conflicting death dates
Various sources give different years: 393, 375, 373, 383, 376 AH. The author quotes multiple historians and then says 'fatammal' (reflect). This shows the challenge of reconciling disparate historical reports.
The death date of the later Abu al-Layth (the faqih) is most consistently around 376 AH, as his book was completed in that year.
3
Distinguish the two Abu al-Layths
The text explicitly states: 'ثم اعلم أن أبا الليث اثنان' (Know that Abu al-Layth is two). The first (the subject of this entry) is titled 'al-Faqih' and died later. The second is 'al-Hafiz' and died in 294 AH. The faqih is younger and authored the fatwa collection al-Nawazil.
The hafiz is an earlier scholar, a hadith expert, while the faqih is a jurist.
4
Note the significance of the book al-Nawazil
The entry concludes by mentioning that his book 'al-Nawazil fi al-Furu'' was dictated in 376 AH, and it contains opinions compiled from Muhammad ibn Shuja'. This work is a major source for later Hanafi fatwa practice.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the importance of al-Nawazil is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

21 - Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: He is Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim, famously known as 'Imam al-Huda'. He studied from Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar from Nasir ibn Yahya from Muhammad ibn Sam'ah from Abu Yusuf. Mawlana 'Abd al-Hayy said: 'The author of Madinat al-'Ulum mentioned his death on Tuesday night, eleven days before the end of Jumada al-Akhirah 393 AH. And the author of al-Kashf mentioned his death when mentioning al-Bustan, al-Tafsir, and Tanbih al-Ghafilin: 375 AH, and when mentioning Sharh al-Jami' 373 AH, and when mentioning Khizanat al-Fiqh 383 AH, and it will come from al-Kafawi that he died 373 AH. I say: It is also mentioned in al-'Uyun and al-Fatawa similar to what is in Khizanat al-Fiqh, and in al-Nawazil: he died 376 AH. So reflect. Then know that Abu al-Layth is two: one is this Abu al-Layth (who is titled 'al-Faqih'), and the second is Abu al-Layth Nasr al-Samarqandi (who is titled 'al-Hafiz'), and the first is later than the second, who died 294 AH. Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This is a detailed biography of Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, known as 'Imam al-Huda'. It gives his full name and chain of transmission. There is confusion about his death date; multiple sources give different years (375, 373, 383, 376, 393). The author, after quoting various opinions, asks the reader to reflect. Then he clarifies that there are two scholars named Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: the faqih (author of al-Nawazil) and the hafiz (earlier, d. 294). The entry ends mid-sentence about his book al-Nawazil, which is continued on the next page.

Key Terms
النوازل (al-nawazil): Legal cases and incidents that occur; a genre of fatwa collections.
الحافظ (al-hafiz): A title used for a scholar with extensive memorization of hadith, distinct from faqih.

Biographical Cross-References (18-20): Identifying Scholars
Very short biographical notes for al-Qarafi, ibn Hayran, and ibn al-Salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scholars referenced (al-Qarafi, ibn Hayran, ibn al-Salah) and explain the purpose of such cross-references in a classical usul al-ifta text.

Core Idea
Cross-references in classical texts are essential for navigating scholarly networks.

This short passage contains three brief biographical notes from a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti. The author identifies scholars by their kunya or full name, providing cross-references to other entries in the book. Such notes serve as indices, helping the reader locate fuller biographical information elsewhere. They also reveal the author's scholarly honesty, as he admits not finding ibn Hayran's biography.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar by kunya or name
Read each entry and note the primary identifier (kunya or name) and the scholar's identity as stated by the author.
e.g. "Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Idris" is al-Qarafi.
2
Recognize the cross-referencing function
Understand that phrases like "سيأتي ذكره" (his mention will come later) and "مر ذكره" (his mention has passed) are directing the reader to other parts of the book.
The author expects the reader to consult the main entry for full biography.
3
Note the author's admission of ignorance
For ibn Hayran, the author states he could not find his biography. This shows the limits of the author's sources and is a sign of scholarly integrity.
The phrase "والله أعلم" (Allah knows best) is used when certainty is lacking.
4
Appreciate the relevance to usul al-ifta
Such footnotes help a mufti trace the authorities behind a ruling. Knowing the school and era of these scholars aids in evaluating the strength of their opinions.
For example, al-Qarafi is a Maliki, ibn al-Salah is a Shafi'i, and ibn Hayran is less known.

Biographical Precision in Hanafi Authority Chains
Biographical corrections and clarifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two distinct figures named 'Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi' and explain the correction of the name 'Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam' to 'Abu al-Nasr Muhammad ibn Sallam' using textual evidence from the passage.

Core Idea
Not every 'Abu al-Layth' is the same: biographical precision preserves the authority of transmission.

The author of the Sharh provides a biographical appendix to clarify the identities of scholars cited in the commentary. This lesson focuses on two critical corrections: distinguishing between two scholars with the same kunya 'Abu al-Layth' and correcting a misattributed name. Mastering such details is essential for every mufti, as the authority of a fatwa often rests on the correct identification of its source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his unique identifier
Read the entry for the scholar. Note the full name (ism, nasab, kunya, laqab) and any nicknames. For example, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi is given as 'Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim' with the laqab 'Imam al-Huda'.
The passage distinguishes two individuals sharing the same kunya.
2
Trace the chain of transmission (mashyakhah)
List the teachers and sources mentioned. For Abu al-Layth, his chain goes back through Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar, Nasir ibn Yahya, Muhammad ibn Sama'a, to Abu Yusuf. This confirms his place in the Hanafi chain.
Teachers indicate the stratum (tabaqah) and reliability.
3
Critically examine reported death dates
Compare the multiple dates mentioned for the scholar's death. For Abu al-Layth, the author lists 373, 375, 376, 383, and 393 AH from various sources. This highlights the need for cross-referencing.
Discrepancies in death dates can affect the chronology of works and teachers.
4
Apply the correction from the passage
For the entry on Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam, the passage argues it is a scribal error. The correct name is Abu al-Nasr Muhammad ibn Sallam. Support comes from his being a contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir and a narrator from Nasir ibn Yahya.
Correcting such errors preserves the integrity of fiqh transmission.

-17- Abu Sulayman al-Juzajani: He is Musa ibn Sulayman, Abu Sulayman al-Juzajani. He took fiqh from Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani) and wrote the books Masail al-Usul and al-Amali. He was a participant with al-Mu'alla ibn Mansur; al-Ma'mun offered him the position of judge but he did not accept. He died after the year 200. He authored al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Nawadir, al-Mabsut, and others.
-18- Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Idris: He is al-Qarafi, whose mention will come later; see al-Qarafi.
19- Abu Ali: He is Ibn Hayran, and I have not found his biography in the books I have, and Allah knows best.
20- Abu Amr: He is Ibn al-Salah, who has been mentioned before.
-21- Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: He is Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim, famously known as "Imam al-Huda". He took from Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar, from Nasir ibn Yahya, from Muhammad ibn Sama'a, from Abu Yusuf. Our master Abd al-Hayy said: "The author of Madinat al-Ulum mentioned his death on Tuesday night, eleven nights having passed from Jumada al-Akhira of the year 393 AH. The author of al-Kashf mentioned his death in connection with al-Bustan, al-Tafsir, and Tanbih al-Ghafilin: in 375 AH; in connection with Sharh al-Jami': 373 AH; in connection with Khizanat al-Fiqh: 383 AH; and it will come from al-Kafawi that he died in 373 AH." I say: It has also been mentioned in al-Uyun and al-Fatawa what was mentioned in Khizanat al-Fiqh, and in al-Nawazil it is mentioned that he died in 376 AH. So ponder. Then know that Abu al-Layth are two: one is this Abu al-Layth (who is nicknamed "al-Faqih") and the second is Abu al-Layth Nasr al-Samarqandi (who is nicknamed "al-Hafiz"). The first is later than the second, who died in 294 AH. His book "al-Nawazil fi al-Furu'" was completed on Friday, a few days after the beginning of Jumada al-Ula in 376 AH. He mentioned that he collected from the statements of Muhammad ibn Shuja'
224
al-Thalji, Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, Muhammad ibn Salama, Nasir ibn Yahya, Muhammad ibn Sallam, Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf, Ali ibn Ahmad al-Farisi, and the faqih Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Abdullah, for they paused to examine the nawazil that occurred to them. He said: I compiled two books from their statements: one is Uyun al-Masail, and the other is al-Nawazil. In al-Uyun I included from the statements of our companions what reached me by narration in these books, and in al-Nawazil I included from the statements of the mashayikh and some statements of our companions who have no narration in the book, to facilitate the way of ijtihad for the reader.
22- Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam: This is how it appears in the copy in my hand, and thus in the copies of Radd al-Muhtar when mentioning the strata of masail. Our master Abd al-Hayy also transmitted it from him in al-Nafi' al-Kabir and did not write anything on it. I have not seen his biography in the books I have, and I think his mention here is not correct. The correct form instead is Abu al-Nasr Muhammad ibn Sallam, who is frequently mentioned in the fatawa along with these scholars. This is supported by the fact that he was a contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir, and among those who narrated from Nasir ibn Yahya, as in al-Jawahir. He is of the high stratum, and other matters that show that he is the correct one. So reflect. His biography in al-Fawaid is worded: Muhammad ibn Sallam Abu Nasr al-Balkhi, sometimes mentioned in fatawa by his name, sometimes by his kunya, and sometimes by both. He is of the high stratum such that they counted him as a contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir. What occurs in some books as Nasr ibn Sallam is an error. The compiler said: "The faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned at the end of his book al-Nawazil that his death was in the year 305 AH."
-23- Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi: He is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Musa Abu al-Yusr, Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. He excelled in the sciences, both furu and usul. The leadership of the Hanafis in Transoxiana ended with him. He was the imam of imams absolutely. He filled the pages with his writings. He died in Bukhara in 493 AH, and his birth was in 421 AH. The verification of al-Bazdawi has already passed in the biography of his brother Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi, so refer to it. Then know that the words of al-Kafawi in the biography
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix from the Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, listing the scholars cited in the commentary with brief details. It serves to identify the authorities behind the rulings and statements referenced throughout the work. The author provides key biographical data: full name, teachers, notable works, and death dates. Notable corrections include the clarification that there are two scholars named Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi—one the Faqih (the author of al-Nawazil, died 376 AH) and the other the Hafiz (died 294 AH). Also, the entry for Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam is corrected to Abu al-Nasr Muhammad ibn Sallam, a high-ranking contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir. The correction is based on cross-referencing with other sources. This information is crucial for students of Hanafi fiqh to assess the authority and transmission chain of a ruling. The compilation method of Abu al-Layth's al-Nawazil is described: he collected opinions of earlier scholars to facilitate ijtihad. The biographical entries reflect the meticulousness of Hanafi scholarship in preserving chains of transmission.

Key Terms
أبو الليث السمرقندي (Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi): Two scholars: (1) Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim, known as Imam al-Huda (al-Faqih), died around 376 AH; (2) Abu al-Layth Nasr al-Samarqandi (al-Hafiz), died 294 AH. The passage distinguishes them.
أبو النصر القاسم بن سلام (Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam): A misnomer corrected to Abu al-Nasr Muhammad ibn Sallam, a Hanafi scholar contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir.
أبو اليسر البزدوي (Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi): Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn, Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 493 AH), leading Hanafi scholar in Transoxiana.

Parsing Biographical Entries: Identifying Scholars and Correcting Errors in Hanafi Sources
Biographical list with corrections and lineage notes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi scholars from their biographical entries, recognize common textual errors, and explain how these entries establish fatwa authority.

Core Idea
Accurate identification of scholars is essential for evaluating the weight of their opinions in Hanafi fatwa.

This passage is a biographical section from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti, listing scholars mentioned in the commentary. As a mufti-in-training, you must learn how to navigate these lists: they are not mere history, but tools for verifying the chain of transmission and the authority level of fatwas. The passage includes key corrections, such as mistaking a scholar's name, and highlights the tabaqa (layer) system that determines whether an opinion is from the 'high class' (al-ṭabaqah al-ʿāliyah) or later authorities.

Guided Path
1
Understand the purpose of biographical lists in Hanafi iftaa
Recognize that such lists help determine the reliability and era of a scholar, which affects the weight of their opinion in fatwa. The author includes corrections (like the mistaken identity of Abu al-Nasr) to avoid errors in attribution.
Biographical entries are part of the mufti's toolkit for 'takhrij' (tracing transmitted opinions).
2
Analyze entry 22: identify the confusion and correction
The text says 'Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Salam' is likely a scribal error; the correct name is 'Muhammad ibn Salam Abu Nasr al-Balkhi'. Note the evidence: he is mentioned alongside peers like Abu Hafs al-Kabir and narrated from Nasir ibn Yahya.
This shows how cross-referencing fatwa collections (like al-Nawazil) and biographical works (like al-Jawahir) resolves errors.
3
Analyze entry 23: recognize the tabaqa and significance of Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi
He is from the 'high class' (al-ṭabaqah al-ʿāliyah), a leading authority in Transoxiana. Note his death year (493 AH) and his master of both usul and furu'. Also note the correction about his grandfather: this refines his lineage and thus his place in the scholarly hierarchy.
Understanding tabaqa helps in assigning authority weight (e.g., his opinions are from the mutaqaddimun, but later than the earliest companions).
4
Examine entry 24: note the role of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf is presented as the first to compile Hanafi works and spread the madhhab. His death year is given as 183 AH (or 182 AH). As a direct student of Abu Hanifa, his opinions are from the highest layer (zahir al-riwaya).
Abu Yusuf's books (al-Kharaj, al-Amali, al-Nawadir) are foundational for Hanafi fatwa.
5
Synthesize: how these entries establish fatwa authority
Each entry provides name, era, teacher/student links, and notable works. The mufti uses this to determine if a transmitted opinion is from a reliable source and at what level of the hierarchy (companions, later authorities, etc.). The corrections (like entry 26, 'al-Majid' vs 'al-Hamid') prevent misattribution.
This parsing exercise builds the skill of 'takhrij al-masa'il' – tracing issues to their original authorities.

الأعلام الوارد ذكرهم في الشرح
٢٢٤
الثلجي، ومحمد بن مقاتل الرازي ومحمد بن سلمة ونصير بن يحيى، ومحمد ابن سلام، وأبى بكر الإسكاف، وعلى بن أحمد الفارسي والفقيه أبي جعفر محمد ابن عبد الله فإنهم وقفوا للنظر فيما وقع لهم من النوازل . قال : وصنفت كتابين من أقاويلهم: : أحدهما: عيون المسائل، والآخر : النوازل، وأوردت في العيون من أقاويل أصحابنا ما وصلنى رواية في هذه الكتب، وفى "النوازل " من أقاويل المشايخ وشيئًا من أقاويل أصحابنا الذين لا رواية عنهم في الكتاب، يسهل على الناظر فيه طريق الاجتهاد " .
٢٢- أبو النصر القاسم بن سلام : هكذا في النسخة التي بيدى، وهكذا في نسخ رد المحتار عند ذكر طبقات المسائل، ونقله أيضا عنه مولانا عبد الحي في النافع الكبير " ولم يكتب عليه شيئًا ، ولم أر ترجمته فيما عندى من الكتب، وظني أن ذكره هنا غير سديد، والصحيح بدله أبو النصر محمد بن سلام الذي كثر ذكره في الفتاوى مع هؤلاء المذكورين، ويؤيد ذلك كونه من أقران أبي حفص الكبير، وممن يروى عن نصير ابن یحیی، كما في "الجواهر" . وكونه من الطبقة العالية وغير ذلك أمور مما يظهر منها أنه هو الصحيح فتدبر وترجمه في الفوائد بما لفظه : محمد بن سلام أبو نصر البلخي تارة يذكر في الفتاوى باسمه وتارة بكنيته وتارة بهما، وهو صاحب الطبقة العالية حتى إنهم عدوه من أقران أبي حفص الكبير. وما وقع في بعض الكتب نصر بن سلام فغلط . قال الجامع : "ذكر الفقيه أبو الليث في آخر كتابه النوازل : أن وفاته كانت سنة ٣٠٥هـ " .
6
-۲۳ - أبو اليسر البزدوي : هو محمد بن محمد بن الحسين بن عبد الكريم ابن موسى أبو اليسر، صدر الإسلام البزدوی، برع في العلوم فروعا وأصولا ، انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية بما وراء النهر، وكان إمام الأئمة على الإطلاق، ملأ بتصانيفه بطون الأوراق، توفى ببخارى سنة ٤٩٣هـ، ومولده سنة ٤٢١هـ . وقد مر تحقيق البزدوي" في ترجمة أخيه فخر الإسلام على البزدوى فلتراجع . ثم أعلم أن كلام الكفوى في ترجمة

٢٢٥
أخيه، وفي ترجمة ولده أحمد بن أبي اليسر محمد بن محمد، وكذا كلامه في ترجمة عبد الكريم بن موسى - كل ذلك نص على أن عبد الكريم جد لفخر الإسلام وأخيه أبى اليسر صدر الإسلام هو مخالف لما ساق غيره ممن يعتمد عليه مما يدل على أنه جد لوالد فخر الإسلام لا لهما، كما ذكره الكفوى، وقد حقق ذلك مولانا عبد الحي في الفوائد. فلتطالع . ٢٤ - أبو يوسف : هو القاضى الإمام يعقوب بن إبراهيم بن حبيب، المقدم من أصحاب الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. ولى قضاء "بغداد" ، فلم يزل بها حتى مات سنة ١٨٣ هـ في خلافة هارون الرشيد. وهو أول من وضع الكتب على مذهب أبي حنيفة، وأملى المسائل ونشرها، وبث علم أبي حنيفة في أقطار الأرض . وله كتاب الخراج ، و "الأمالي"، و "النوادر" ، كذا في "الفوائد" . وفي الكشف عند ذكر كتاب الخراج و المبسوط " : أنه توفى سنة ١٨٢هـ.
٢٥ - أحمد الحموي : هو السيد أحمد بن محمد الحنفى الحموي من تلامذة حسن الشرنبلالي، صاحب نور الإيضاح، وله حاشية على الأشباه سماها "غمز عيون البصائر في شرح الأشباه والنظائر أوله : لك الحمد يا من تنزهت ذاتك عن الأشباه والنظائر كذا ظهر لي عن مطالعة الكتب .
٢٦ الأمير المجيد : كذا في النسخة التي بيدى . والمذكور في الفوائد البهية والجواهر المضيئة، وأنساب السمعاني : بدله الحميد لا المجيد. فتدبر .
ی
٢٧ الباجي : هو القاضي أبو الوليد سليمان بن خلف بن سعد بن أيوب ابن وارث التجيبي (بضم التاء وكسر الجيم، نسبة إلى قبيلة من كندة الأندلسي القرطبي، من أعيان الطبقة العاشرة من العلماء المالكية، المولود سنة ٤٠٣هـ ، والمتوفى
The notable figures mentioned in the commentary. (224) Al-Thalji, Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, Muhammad ibn Salama, Nasir ibn Yahya, Muhammad ibn Salam, Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf, Ali ibn Ahmad al-Farisi, and the jurist Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Abdullah — they stopped to deliberate on the incidents that occurred to them. He said: I compiled two books from their statements: one is 'Uyun al-Masa'il, and the other is al-Nawazil. In 'Uyun I included from the statements of our companions what reached me through narration in these books, and in al-Nawazil I included from the statements of the shaykhs and some from the statements of our companions who have no narration in the books, to ease the path of ijtihad for the one who looks into it. (22) Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Salam: Thus in the copy in my hand, and thus in the copies of Radd al-Muhtar when mentioning the layers of issues, and Mulla Abd al-Hayy also transmitted from him in al-Nafi' al-Kabir, and he did not write anything on it, and I did not see his biography in the books I have, and I think his mention here is not correct, and the correct replacement is Abu al-Nasr Muhammad ibn Salam, who is frequently mentioned in the fatwas with these mentioned scholars, and this is supported by his being a contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir, and among those who narrated from Nasir ibn Yahya, as in al-Jawahir, and his being of the high class, and other matters that indicate that he is the correct one, so reflect. His biography in al-Fawa'id states: Muhammad ibn Salam Abu Nasr al-Balkhi — sometimes mentioned in fatwas by his name, sometimes by his kunya, sometimes by both, and he is of the high class, so much so that they counted him among the peers of Abu Hafs al-Kabir. What occurs in some books as Nasr ibn Salam is a mistake. The compiler said: The jurist Abu al-Layth mentioned in the end of his book al-Nawazil that his death was in 305 AH. (23) Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi: He is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Musa, Abu al-Yusr, Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. He excelled in the sciences, both branches and principles. The leadership of the Hanafis in Transoxiana ended with him, and he was the imam of imams absolutely, filling the folds of papers with his works. He died in Bukhara in 493 AH, and his birth was in 421 AH. The investigation of al-Bazdawi has been mentioned in the biography of his brother Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi, so refer back. Then know that the statement of al-Kafawi in the biography of his brother, and in the biography of his son Ahmad ibn Abi al-Yusr Muhammad ibn Muhammad, and likewise his statement in the biography of Abd al-Karim ibn Musa — all of that indicates that Abd al-Karim is the grandfather of Fakhr al-Islam and his brother Abu al-Yusr Sadr al-Islam, which contradicts what others who are relied upon have stated, indicating that he is the grandfather of the father of Fakhr al-Islam, not of them both, as al-Kafawi mentioned. Mulla Abd al-Hayy has verified that in al-Fawa'id, so consult it. (24) Abu Yusuf: He is the judge, the imam, Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim ibn Habib, the foremost among the companions of the Great Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. He was appointed judge of Baghdad and remained there until he died in 183 AH during the caliphate of Harun al-Rashid. He was the first to compose books on the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, dictated the issues, spread them, and disseminated the knowledge of Abu Hanifa throughout the lands. He has the book al-Kharaj, al-Amali, and al-Nawadir, as in al-Fawa'id. In al-Kashf, when mentioning the book al-Kharaj and al-Mabsut, it is stated that he died in 182 AH. (25) Ahmad al-Hamawi: He is Sayyid Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Hanafi al-Hamawi, a student of Hasan al-Shurunbulali, author of Nur al-Idah. He has a gloss on al-Ashbah called 'Ghamz 'Uyun al-Basa'ir fi Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.' Its opening: 'Praise be to You, O He whose essence is transcendent above likenesses and parallels.' This appeared to me from reading the books. (26) Al-Amir al-Majid: Thus in the copy in my hand. What is mentioned in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, and Ansab al-Sam'ani is instead 'al-Hamid' not 'al-Majid.' So reflect. (27) Al-Baji: He is the judge Abu al-Walid Sulayman ibn Khalaf ibn Sa'd ibn Ayyub ibn Warith al-Tujibi (with damma on ta and kasra on jim, attribution to a tribe from Kinda), the Andalusian, the Cordoban, one of the notable figures of the tenth class of Maliki scholars, born in 403 AH, and died
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti, listing the notable scholars referenced in the commentary. It begins with a list of earlier Hanafi jurists (e.g., al-Thalji, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, etc.) who devoted themselves to deliberating on new cases (nawazil). The author notes that he compiled two works from their sayings: 'Uyun al-Masa'il (Essentials of Issues) and al-Nawazil (Incidents), to facilitate ijtihad. Entry 22 discusses confusion over the identity of 'Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Salam'. The author argues this is a scribal error; the correct scholar is Muhammad ibn Salam Abu Nasr al-Balkhi, a contemporary of Abu Hafs al-Kabir who died in 305 AH. Entry 23 gives a biography of Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi (d. 493 AH), a leading Hanafi scholar from Transoxiana who wrote extensively. A correction is noted regarding his lineage: contrary to al-Kafawi, his grandfather Abd al-Karim is the grandfather of his father, not of him and his brother. Entry 24 covers Abu Yusuf (d. 183 or 182 AH), the chief disciple of Abu Hanifa, first to write Hanafi works, and judge of Baghdad. Entry 25 is about Ahmad al-Hamawi, a student of al-Shurunbulali, author of a gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. Entry 26 notes a variant reading: 'al-Amir al-Hamid' not 'al-Majid'. Entry 27 identifies al-Baji, a Maliki scholar (d. 474 AH), included for cross-reference. This material helps students understand the chain of authorities and works in Hanafi fatwa literature.

Key Terms
النوازل (al-nawāzil): Incidents or new cases that require legal ruling, often compiled as fatwa collections.
الطبقة العالية (al-ṭabaqah al-ʿāliyah): The high class of scholars, i.e., the earliest generations of Hanafi jurists close to the founders.
عيون المسائل ('uyūn al-masā'il): The Essentials of Issues, a work compiling key opinions from early Hanafi scholars.
قاضي القضاة (qāḍī al-quḍāh): Chief judge; a title held by Abu Yusuf as the first to hold this position in Baghdad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is correctly identified as the author of the first compiled books on the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi

Key Takeaway
Biographical entries are not mere records; they are essential tools for verifying the authenticity and authority of transmitted opinions in Hanafi fatwa.

Life of the Author

Identifying Hanafi Authorities in the Commentary
Biographical sketches of referenced scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholars mentioned in the commentary, state their madhhab affililation, and correct common textual errors in biographical entries.

Core Idea
Accurate biography ensures correct attribution and reliable fatwa transmission.

In Hanafi iftaa, knowing the authorities cited in commentaries is essential. This biographical appendix lists key scholars – Hanafi, Maliki, and Shafi'i – and clarifies textual errors regarding names and dates. By mastering this list, you strengthen your ability to trace a fatwa back to its source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar's Name and Status
Each entry begins with a name and sometimes a laqab (honorific). Note whether the scholar is a companion of Abu Hanifa, a later commentator, or from another madhhab.
Example: 'Abu Yusuf' is a direct student; 'al-Baji' is Maliki.
2
Note the Madhhab and Role
Some entries explicitly state madhhab (e.g., 'al-Hanafi', 'al-Maliki'). Others are known from context. Also note their role: judge, biographer, commentator.
Ahmad al-Hamawi is Hanafi; al-Baji is Maliki; al-Burhan al-Anbasi is Shafi'i.
3
Check the Death Date and Source
The text often gives death dates from 'al-Kashf' or other works. Compare multiple sources if possible. The entry for al-Tamimi shows a date correction from 190 H to 1010 H.
Always verify death dates as copyist errors are common.
4
Identify Textual Corrections
The author explicitly corrects a misprint: 'al-Majid' should be 'al-Hamid' (entry 26). Also corrects a death year for al-Tamimi. These are important for reliable referencing.
Such corrections prevent attribution errors.
5
Cross-reference with Biographical Works
The author references works like 'al-Fawa'id', 'Kashf al-Zunun', and 'Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya'. Knowing these sources allows you to independently verify the information.
E.g., 'al-Kashf' (Kashf al-Zunun) by Haji Khalifa.

-۲۸ - البرهان الأنباسي : هو من أقران ابن الهمام، كما ذكره صاحب العقود، وعلى هذا يكون من رجال المائة التاسعة. والله أعلم بالصواب. ثم رأيت السيوطى ترجم للبرهان الأنباسي في "حسن المحاضرة" وقال : "البرهان الأنباسي إبراهيم بن موسى ابن أيوب الورع الزاهد المحقق، شيخ الشيوخ بالديار المصرية . ولد سنة خمس وعشرين وسبعمائة، وأخذ عن الأسنوى وغيره. وله تصانيف، وولّى مشيخة سعيد السعداء وعين القضاء الشافعية فاختفى. وكان مشهوراً بالصلاح، تقرأ عليه الجن. مات في المحرم سنة اثنتين وثمانمائة راجعا من الحج، ودفن بعيون القصب، ورثاه الحافظ زين الدين العراقي

This is what appeared to me from reviewing books. 26 - al-Amir al-Majid: Thus in the copy in my hand. And what is mentioned in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya and al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a and Ansab al-Sam'ani: instead of it is al-Hamid, not al-Majid. So reflect. 27 - al-Baji: He is the judge Abu al-Walid Sulayman ibn Khalaf ibn Sa'd ibn Ayyub ibn Warith al-Tujibi (with dammah on the ta and kasr on the jim, a nisbah to a tribe of Kinda), the Andalusian, the Cordoban, one of the notables of the tenth generation of Maliki scholars, born in 403 AH and died in 494 AH. He held judgeships in places in al-Andalus. It is said: Among the Malikis after Judge Abd al-Wahhab, there is none like al-Baji. Ibn Farhun said: Their origin is from Badajoz, then to Baja, meaning Baja of al-Andalus, and then there is another Baja in the city of Ifriqiya, and another Baja in the land of Isfahan in the non-Arab lands, as in the introduction of al-Awjaz. And the author of al-Kashf mentioned when discussing the commentators of al-Muwatta that he died in 474 AH. 28 - al-Burhan al-Anbasi: He is one of the contemporaries of Ibn al-Humam, as mentioned by the author of al-'Uqud, and accordingly he is from the men of the ninth century. Allah knows best the truth. Then I saw al-Suyuti translated al-Burhan al-Anbasi in Husn al-Muhadara and said: 'Al-Burhan al-Anbasi is Ibrahim ibn Musa ibn Ayyub the pious, ascetic, verifier, the shaykh of shaykhs in the Egyptian lands. He was born in 725 AH, and studied under al-Isnawi and others. He has writings, and he was appointed as shaykh of Sa'id al-Su'ada and designated for the Shafi'i judgeship, so he went into hiding. He was famous for righteousness; the jinn would recite the Quran before him. He died in Muharram 802 AH while returning from Hajj, and was buried at 'Uyun al-Qasab, and was eulogized by the memorizer Zain al-Din al-'Iraqi.' 29 - al-Tamimi: He is the judge Taqi al-Din ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Tamimi, al-Gharri, al-Hanafi, author of al-Tabaqat, the virtuous scholar, the literary man. He studied under many scholars, entered the Roman lands, authored and well composed the Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya, in which he collected a number of scholars of the Roman lands and their leaders. Al-Hafaji praised him greatly in Rayhanat al-Athara. He died in Egypt on Saturday, the fifth of Jumada al-Thani in the year 190 H, while in the prime of youth, as in Murr al-Amathil quoting from Khulasat al-Athar, but his statement: year 190 H is distorted, as is not hidden, and apparently he died in the year 1010 H (1005 H? actually five and one thousand), as mentioned in al-Kashf in several places. And the fact that it is distorted can be deduced from what the author of al-Kashf said when mentioning Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya: that he wrote a large book compiling the biographies of the Hanafis, comprehensive and excellent, and it is the greatest book written on the biographies of the people
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix listing notable scholars referenced in the main commentary. It begins with a clarification about the lineage of Abd al-Karim, confirming he is the grandfather of Fakhr al-Islam's father, not of Fakhr al-Islam himself, a point verified by Mawlana Abd al-Hayy. The first major entry (entry 24) is for Abu Yusuf (d. 183/182 AH), the distinguished student of Abu Hanifa and first to formally compile Hanafi fiqh. The text notes his works and his pioneering role. Next (entry 25) is Ahmad al-Hamawi (d. after 1098 AH?), a Hanafi scholar and glossator of the Ashbah. Entry 26 corrects a copyist error: 'al-Majid' should be 'al-Hamid'. Entry 27 covers the Maliki judge al-Baji (d. 494 AH), with details on his lineage and reputation. Entry 28 introduces al-Burhan al-Anbasi (d. 802 AH), a Shafi'i scholar and contemporary of Ibn al-Humam. Finally, entry 29 discusses al-Tamimi (d. ca. 1010 AH), a Hanafi biographer. The text notes a significant misprint in his death year, correcting it from 190 AH to 1010 AH. This section serves as a reference for identifying the authorities cited in the main commentary.

Key Terms
الأعلام (al-a'lām): Notable figures; specifically, the scholars whose biographies are listed.
الكشف (al-kashf): Likely refers to 'Kashf al-Zunun' by Haji Khalifa, a bibliographic encyclopedia. The text uses it as a source for death dates.
الطبقات الحنفية (al-ṭabaqāt al-ḥanafiyya): A biographical work by al-Tamimi classifying Hanafi scholars by generation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ahmad al-Hamawi

C) al-Baji
D) al-Tamimi

Key Takeaway
Accurate biographical knowledge of cited authorities ensures correct attribution and strengthens the reliability of a fatwa.

Al-Burhan al-Anbasi: The Peer of Ibn al-Humam
Biographical snapshot of a 9th-century Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Burhan al-Anbasi as a key Hanafi authority from the 9th century and explain why his biographical details are relevant for fatwa verification.

Core Idea
A scholar's era and contemporaries determine the weight of his transmission.

This short biographical entry introduces al-Burhan al-Anbasi, a Hanafi scholar and contemporary of Ibn al-Humam. For a mufti, knowing when and where a scholar lived helps assess the authority of his legal opinions. This lesson will help you place al-Burhan in the Hanafi chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Who is al-Burhan al-Anbasi? State his full name (Ibrahim ibn Musa ibn Ayyub), his birth year (725 AH) and death year (802 AH), and his notable qualities (pious, ascetic, verifying scholar, shaykh of shaykhs).
Note his lineage and the title 'al-Burhan'.
2
Establish his relationship to Ibn al-Humam
The author calls him a 'peer' (qiran) of Ibn al-Humam. Ibn al-Humam is a towering Hanafi authority (d. 861 AH). Being his peer means al-Burhan was contemporaneous and of similar scholarly rank, which elevates his transmitted opinions.
Ibn al-Humam's works are core to the later Hanafi school; peers' views carry weight.
3
Extract relevant details for fatwa
Which details from the biography influence the reliability of his transmitted opinions? His teaching post (shaykh of Sa'id al-Su'ada), his authored works, his piety (which bolsters trust), and his association with al-Isnavi (a Shafi'i scholar) indicate his breadth. Also, his hiding from the Shafi'i judgeship shows he remained loyal to the Hanafi school.
The mention that jinn recited before him is a sign of extreme piety, not a legal factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الأنباسي : هو من أقران ابن الهمام، كما ذكره صاحب العقود، وعلى هذا يكون من رجال المائة التاسعة. والله أعلم بالصواب. ثم رأيت السيوطى ترجم للبرهان الأنباسي في "حسن المحاضرة" وقال : "البرهان الأنباسي إبراهيم بن موسى ابن أيوب الورع الزاهد المحقق، شيخ الشيوخ بالديار المصرية . ولد سنة خمس وعشرين وسبعمائة، وأخذ عن الأسنوى وغيره. وله تصانيف، وولّى مشيخة سعيد السعداء وعين القضاء الشافعية فاختفى. وكان مشهوراً بالصلاح، تقرأ عليه الجن. مات في المحرم سنة اثنتين وثمانمائة راجعا من الحج، ودفن بعيون القصب، ورثاه الحافظ زين الدين العراقي"
Al-Burhan al-Anbasi: He was among the peers of Ibn al-Humam, as mentioned by the author of al-'Uqud, and on this basis he is from the men of the ninth century. And Allah knows best what is correct. Then I saw al-Suyuti translate Al-Burhan al-Anbasi in 'Husn al-Muhadara' and said: 'Al-Burhan al-Anbasi Ibrahim ibn Musa ibn Ayyub, the pious, ascetic, verifier, the shaykh of shaykhs in the Egyptian lands. He was born in the year 725, and studied under al-Isnavi and others. He authored works, and was appointed as the shaykh of Sa'id al-Su'ada' and the judgeship of the Shafi'is but he went into hiding. He was famous for righteousness, and the jinn used to recite the Quran before him. He died in Muharram of the year 802, returning from Hajj, and was buried at 'Uyun al-Qasab, and was eulogized by al-Hafiz Zayn al-Din al-Iraqi.'
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for al-Burhan al-Anbasi, a Hanafi scholar from the ninth century AH. It first notes that he was a contemporary of Ibn al-Humam (d. 861/1457), placing him in the ninth century. Then it quotes al-Suyuti's biography, which gives his full name and describes him as a pious, ascetic, and verifying scholar, a shaykh of shaykhs in Egypt. He was born in 725/1325 and studied under al-Isnavi (a Shafi'i scholar). He authored works and was appointed to a teaching post and judgeship but went into hiding. He was so righteous that the jinn recited the Quran before him. He died in 802/1399-1400 returning from Hajj and was buried at 'Uyun al-Qasab. This entry provides key biographical details for a Hanafi scholar who is referenced in later works.

Key Terms
البرهان الأنباسي (al-Burhan al-Anbasi): A Hanafi scholar of the ninth century AH, known for piety and as a peer of Ibn al-Humam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 725 AH
B) 802 AH
C) 801 AH
D) 800 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Burhan al-Anbasi was a peer of Ibn al-Humam, placing him among the 9th-century Hanafi authorities whose biographies are essential for verifying transmitted opinions.

Al-Tamimi and His Tabaqat: A Key Biographical Source
Biographical entry for a Hanafi scholar and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Tamimi's full name, his major work, and correct the common error about his death year.

Core Idea
Al-Tamimi's Tabaqat is the greatest collection of Hanafi biographies, completed in 993 AH.

Biographical works (tabaqat) are essential for understanding the transmission and authority of Hanafi rulings. This entry introduces al-Tamimi, a Hanafi judge who compiled a monumental dictionary of Hanafi scholars. It also illustrates how later scholars correct errors in earlier sources—a key skill for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar’s full name and lineage
Extract the complete name: Taqi al-Din ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Tamimi al-Gharri al-Hanafi. Notice the nisbas indicating place and madhhab.
Al-Tamimi is a Hanafi judge and literary figure.
2
Note his scholarly activities
He studied under many scholars, traveled to the Roman lands (Rum), and authored a book on the Tabaqat of Hanafis.
His travels allowed him to document scholars from different regions.
3
Identify his major work
The work is 'al-Tabaqat al-Sunniyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya'. It covers Hanafi scholars up to his time, including those from al-Shaqa'iq and later.
This work is considered the greatest book on Hanafi biographies.
4
Resolve the death year discrepancy
The text first gives a wrong year (190 AH) but corrects it using al-Kashf: he died around 1005 AH, completing his Tabaqat in 993 AH.
Understanding how scholars correct errors is vital for verifying sources.
5
Assess the significance for Hanafi studies
Al-Tamimi’s Tabaqat is a primary source for identifying authoritative Hanafi scholars and their chains (sanad).
Muftis rely on such works to weigh opinions and determine mufta bihi positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التميمي : هو القاضي تقى الدين بن عبد القادر التيمي، الغرى، الحنفي، صاحب ،الطبقات العالم الفاضل، الأديب، أخذ عن علماء كثيرين، ودخل الروم وألف وأحسن تأليف طبقات الحنفية ، جمع فيها جملة من علماء الروم ورؤساءها، وأثنى عليه الحفاجي في ريحانته كثيراً. نوفى بمصر في يوم السبت، خامس جمادى الآخرة سنة ١٩٠هـ ، وهو في سن الكهوله، كذا فى مر الأماثل " نقلا عن خلاصة الأثر"، لكن قوله : سنة ١٩٠هـ محرف، كما لا يخفى، والظاهر أنه توفى سنة ٥ ١٠٠هـ (خمس وألف)، كما هو المذكور في الكشف في عدة مواضع . ويستفاد كونه محرفًا مما قاله صاحب الكشف منذ ذكر طبقات الحنفية : من أنه صنف فى ذلك كتاباً كبيراً جمع فيه تراجم الحنفية، فأوعى وأجاد وهو أجل الكتب المؤلفة في تراجم أهل الرأى أدرج فيه رجال الشقائق ومن بعده إلى زمنه وأتمه سنة ٩٩٣هـ، وسماه الطبقات السنية في تراجم الحنفية .
Al-Tamimi: He is the judge Taqi al-Din ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Tamimi, al-Gharri, al-Hanafi, author of al-Tabaqat, the virtuous scholar, the literary man. He studied under many scholars, entered the Roman lands and authored and excelled in authoring the Tabaqat of the Hanafis, in which he collected a group of scholars of the Romans and their leaders. Al-Hafaji praised him much in his Rayhana. He died in Egypt on Saturday, the fifth of Jumada al-Akhira of the year 190 AH, and he was in middle age. So it is in Mar al-Amthal, quoting from Khulasat al-Athar, but his statement: 'year 190 AH' is distorted, as is not hidden, and it appears that he died in the year 5 1000 AH (five and a thousand), as mentioned in al-Kashf in several places. And the fact that it is distorted is understood from what the author of al-Kashf said when mentioning the Tabaqat of the Hanafis: that he authored in that a great book in which he collected biographies of Hanafis, comprehensively and excellently, and it is the greatest book authored in the biographies of the people of ra'y; he included in it the men of al-Shaqa'iq and after it up to his time, and completed it in the year 993 AH, and named it al-Tabaqat al-Sunniyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for al-Tamimi, a Hanafi judge and author of a biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars. It notes his full name and that he studied with many scholars and traveled to the Roman regions. He wrote a book on the Tabaqat of Hanafis, praised by al-Hafaji. The entry discusses the confusion over his death year: one source says 190 AH, but the author corrects this by citing al-Kashf which states he died around 1005 AH, noting that his major work 'al-Tabaqat al-Sunniyya' was completed in 993 AH. This places him in the late 10th/early 11th century AH. The biography identifies him as a key historian of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الطبقات السنية في تراجم الحنفية (al-Tabaqat al-Sunniyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya): The major biographical work by al-Tamimi covering Hanafi scholars up to his time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the name of al-Tamimi's famous biographical work?
A) Mar al-Amthal
B) Khulasat al-Athar
C) al-Tabaqat al-Sunniyya
D) al-Shaqa'iq

Key Takeaway
Al-Tamimi's Tabaqat al-Sunniyya is the most comprehensive biographical source for Hanafi scholars, completed in 993 AH.

Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi: Hanafi Scholar and Author of al-Mughni fi al-Usul
Biographical entry of a Hanafi scholar, author of al-Mughni fi al-Usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly chain of al-Khabbazi and reconcile the conflicting death years using source criticism.

Core Idea
A scholar's isnad is his credential; a discrepancy in death years demands tarjih through evidence.

This biographical entry introduces Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi, a key figure in Hanafi usul. His chain of teachers connects him directly to the author of al-Hidayah. Understanding his scholarly lineage and the dispute over his death year is essential for evaluating his works and their authority in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Find the full name of Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi and his most famous work mentioned in the passage.
His work is al-Mughni fi al-Usul.
2
Trace the scholarly chain
List the teachers from al-Khabbazi back to the author of al-Hidayah in order.
Chain: al-Khabbazi ← Ala al-Din al-Bukhari ← Fakhr al-Din al-Ma'aymiraghi ← Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari ← Sahib al-Hidayah.
3
Note students and activities
Identify his students and his travels mentioned in the passage.
He taught in Damascus, performed Hajj, and had students like al-Qunawi.
4
Examine death year discrepancy
Identify the two different death years given and the sources for each.
al-Fawa'id says 691 AH; al-Kashf says 671 AH.
5
Reconcile the dates
Use the evidence of the gloss on al-Hidayah to determine which death year is more likely.
The gloss by al-Qunawi, completed after al-Khabbazi's death, supports 691 as the later date.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جلال الدين الخبازى هو عمر بن محمد بن عـمـر جلال الدین الخبازي، صاحب المغني في الأصول، كان عالما، زاهدا، متنسكا، جامعا للفروع والأصول، أخذ عن علاء الدين عبد العزيز البخاري عن فخر الدين محمد المايمرغى عن شمس الأئمة محمد بن عبد الستار الكردري عن صاحب الهداية، وبلغ رتبة الكمال، ثم قدم الدمشق ودرس وأفتى وحج ، وأخذ عنه أبو العباس أحمد بن مسعود بن عبدالرحمن القونوي والبدر الطويل، وداود الرومى المنطقى، وهبة الله بن أحمد التركستاني مات سنة إحدى وتسعين وستمائة، كذا في الفوائد، وفيه أيضا قال الجامع : أرخ صاحب الكشف وفاته سنة إحدى وسبعين وستمائة حيث قال : المغنى في أصول الفقه للشيخ جلال الدين عمر بن محمد الخبازى الخجندى الحنفى المتوفى سنة إحدى وسبعين وستمائة . أقول : وأرّخ عند ذكر شروح الهداية سنة إحدى وتسعين وستمائة حيث قال : وللشيخ جلال الدين عمر بن محمد الخبازي، المتوفى سنة إحدى وتسعين وستمائة - حاشية مشهورة، أخذها محمد بن أحمد القونوي وكملها إلى آخر الهداية وسماها تكملة الفوائد
Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi is Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Umar Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi, author of al-Mughni fi al-Usul. He was a scholar, ascetic, devoted, combining furu' and usul. He studied under Ala al-Din Abd al-Aziz al-Bukhari, from Fakhr al-Din Muhammad al-Ma'aymiraghi, from Shams al-A'immah Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari, from the author of al-Hidayah, and attained the rank of perfection. Then he came to Damascus, taught, issued fatwa, and performed Hajj. His students include Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Mas'ud ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Qunawi, al-Badr al-Tawil, Dawud al-Rumi al-Mantiqi, and Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad al-Turkistani. He died in the year 691 AH, as in al-Fawa'id. In it also the compiler said: The author of al-Kashf recorded his death as 671 AH, saying: 'al-Mughni fi Usul al-Fiqh by Shaykh Jalal al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad al-Khabbazi al-Khujandi al-Hanafi, died 671 AH.' I say: And he recorded in the section of commentaries on al-Hidayah the year 691 AH, saying: 'And for Shaykh Jalal al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad al-Khabbazi, died 691 AH, a famous gloss, taken by Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Qunawi who completed it to the end of al-Hidayah and called it Takmilat al-Fawa'id.'
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi, a Hanafi scholar and author of al-Mughni fi al-Usul. It gives his full name and describes him as a combined expert in furu' (branches) and usul (principles). His scholarly chain is notable: he studied under Ala al-Din al-Bukhari, through several intermediaries, linking to the author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani). He taught in Damascus and performed Hajj. The passage discusses a discrepancy in his death year: some sources say 691 AH, while al-Kashf says 671 AH. The author notes that al-Kashf also mentions a famous gloss (hashiya) on al-Hidayah by al-Khabbazi, completed by al-Qunawi and called Takmilat al-Fawa'id, which supports the later date. This entry shows the importance of verifying biographical data from multiple sources.

Key Terms
المغني في الأصول (al-Mughni fi al-Usul): A well-known work on usul al-fiqh by al-Khabbazi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Al-Hidayah

Key Takeaway
Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi's scholarly chain links him to the Hidayah author, and his death year is most likely 691 AH based on the evidence of his gloss on al-Hidayah.

Biographical Entry: Al-Hakim al-Shahid
Biographical entry of a Hanafi scholar and judge who died a martyr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly role of al-Hakim al-Shahid and explain his significance in Hanafi intellectual history.

Core Idea
A judge, a vizier, a martyr — al-Hakim al-Shahid bridges Hanafi law and governance.

This lesson introduces al-Hakim al-Shahid, a classical Hanafi authority whose life exemplified the integration of legal scholarship and state service. Though the biographical note is brief, it anchors his identity as a key transmitter in the Zahir al-Riwayah tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person
Al-Hakim al-Shahid is Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi al-Balkhi, a Hanafi scholar. His lineage shows deep roots in the Hanafi tradition.
2
Note his positions
He was appointed as a judge in Bukhara and later as vizier to the governor of Khurasan. This shows the trust placed in him by the political authorities.
3
Understand his martyrdom
He was killed in Rabi' al-Thani 344 AH (955 CE), earning the title 'al-Shahid'. His martyrdom adds to his reverence in the Hanafi school.
The entry is incomplete; it begins a citation from al-Kashf that is cut off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاكم الشهيد : هو أبو الفضل محمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن عبد الله ابن عبد المجيد بن إسماعيل بن الحاكم الشهير بالحاكم الشهيد المروزى البلخي، ولّى القضاء ببخارا، ثم ولاه الأمير صاحب خراسان وزارته، وقتل شهيدا في ربيع الآخر سنة ٣٤٤هـ، كذا في الفوائد البهية، وفى الأنساب والجواهر المضيئة، والكشف : أنه
Al-Hakim al-Shahid: He is Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abd Allah ibn Abd al-Majid ibn Isma'il ibn al-Hakim, famous as al-Hakim al-Shahid al-Marwazi al-Balkhi. He was appointed judgeship in Bukhara, then the governor of Khurasan appointed him as his vizier, and he was killed as a martyr in Rabi' al-Thani of the year 344 AH. So it is in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, and in al-Ansab and al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, and al-Kashf: that he...

It gives his full name and lineage, noting he was a judge in Bukhara and later vizier to the governor of Khurasan. He was martyred in 344 AH (955 CE). The entry cites al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, al-Ansab, and al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, and begins a citation from al-Kashf but is cut off. Despite being incomplete, it identifies him as a significant Hanafi figure who held high judicial and administrative positions and died a martyr.

Key Terms
الحاكم الشهيد (al-Hakim al-Shahid): Title for Abu al-Fadl al-Marwazi, a Hanafi judge and martyr.

Biography of Al-Hakim al-Shahid: Lessons on Textual Integrity
Biography of a Hanafi scholar and judge who was martyred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the life and contributions of al-Hakim al-Shahid and explain the moral lesson about tampering with foundational texts.

Core Idea
Tampering with the core texts of the madhhab can have severe consequences, as seen in the tragic story of al-Hakim al-Shahid.

Al-Hakim al-Shahid was a brilliant Hanafi scholar and judge whose legacy is marked by both his scholarly contributions and his tragic martyrdom. His story contains a profound lesson for any mufti about the sanctity of the transmitted texts. In this lesson, we explore his biography and the cautionary tale surrounding his abridgment of Imam Muhammad's works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and positions
Read the opening to know his lineage, that he was a judge in Bukhara, and later minister to the ruler of Khurasan.
His title 'al-Shahid' indicates he died as a martyr.
2
Note the conflicting accounts of his death
The text gives two possible years: 344 AH or 334 AH. Recognize that such discrepancies are common in early biographical sources.
The author of this text (likely al-Qari) favors 334 AH as will come later.
3
Understand his role as a hadith memorizer and teacher
He memorized sixty thousand hadith and taught many scholars, including al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. This shows his expertise in hadith as well as fiqh.
His hadith mastery strengthens his authority as a faqih.
4
Analyze the dream story and its moral
The story relates that he abridged Imam Muhammad's books, and in a dream Imam Muhammad cursed him, leading to his gruesome death. This is a cautionary tale about altering the transmitted texts of the madhhab.
Whether literal or symbolic, the story underscores the gravity of tampering with foundational works.
5
Recognize the authority of his books in the Hanafi school
Despite the tragic end, his books al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa are considered foundational after the books of Imam Muhammad. They are reliable sources for fatwa.
These works are part of the post-Zahir al-Riwayah corpus but retain high authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاكم الشهيد : هو أبو الفضل محمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن عبد الله ابن عبد المجيد بن إسماعيل بن الحاكم الشهير بالحاكم الشهيد المروزى البلخي، ولّى القضاء ببخارا، ثم ولاه الأمير صاحب خراسان وزارته، وقتل شهيدا في ربيع الآخر سنة ٣٤٤هـ، كذا في الفوائد البهية، وفى الأنساب والجواهر المضيئة، والكشف : أنه قتل سنة ٣٣٤هـ ، وبه قال المصنف كما سيأتي . ودفن بـ 'مرو' برأس مقبرة 'سوركدان' ، كما في الجواهر . وسمع الحديث بمرو على أبي رجاء محمد بن حمدويه (وهو يروى عن أحمد بن حنبل وغيره) وسمع منه أئمة خراسان وحفاظها قاطبة منهم : أبو عبد الله الحاكم الحافظ صاحب المستدرك ، وكان يحفظ ستين ألفا من حديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم . وفى الأشباه نقلا عن تلقيح المحبوبي : أنه قال حين ابتلى بمحنة القتل بمرو من جهة الأتراك : 'هذه جزاء من آثر الدنيا على الآخرة، والعالم متى أخفى علمه وترك حقه خيف عليه أن يمتحن بمايسوؤه . وقيل : كان سبب ذلك أنه لما رأى في كتب محمد مکررات وتطويلات خلسها وحذف مكررها فرأی محمد رحمه الله في منامه، فقال: لما فعلت هذا بكتبي؟ ' فقال : 'لأن فى الفقهاء كسالى فحذفت المكرر، وذكرت المقرر تسهيلا فغضب وقال : 'قطعك الله كما قطعت كتبي ' . فابتلى بالأتراك حتى جعلوه على رأس شجرتين فتقطع نصفين ' . وكتابه 'الكافي' و'المنتقى ' أصلان من أصول المذهب بعد كتب محمد رحمه الله ، وهما يدلان على كمال فضله وتبحره في الفقه .
Al-Hakim al-Shahid: He is Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abd Allah ibn Abd al-Majid ibn Isma'il ibn al-Hakim, famous as al-Hakim al-Shahid al-Marwazi al-Balkhi. He became judge in Bukhara, then the Amir of Khurasan appointed him as his minister. He was killed as a martyr in Rabi' al-Akhar in 344 AH, as in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah, and in al-Ansab and al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah and al-Kashf: that he was killed in 334 AH, and the author (of this book) says so as will come. He was buried in Marw at the entrance of the 'Surkdan' cemetery, as in al-Jawahir. He heard hadith in Marw from Abu Raja' Muhammad ibn Hamdawayh (who narrated from Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others). From him heard the imams of Khurasan and all its hadith scholars, among them Abu Abd Allah al-Hakim al-Hafiz, author of al-Mustadrak. He memorized sixty thousand hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). In al-Ashbah, quoting from Talqih al-Mahbubi: He said when he was afflicted with the ordeal of being killed in Marw at the hands of the Turks: 'This is the recompense of one who preferred this world over the Hereafter. When a scholar conceals his knowledge and abandons his right, it is feared that he will be tested with what distresses him.' It is said that the reason was that when he saw in the books of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) repetitions and lengthy passages, he abridged them and removed repetitions. Then he saw Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) in a dream, who said: 'Why did you do this to my books?' He replied: 'Because among the jurists are lazy ones, so I removed repetitions and mentioned the established (rulings) for ease.' So Muhammad became angry and said: 'May Allah cut you as you cut my books.' So he was afflicted by the Turks until they tied him between two trees and he was torn in half. His books 'al-Kafi' and 'al-Muntaqa' are two foundational works of the school after the books of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), and they indicate the perfection of his virtue and his deep knowledge of fiqh.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage gives the biography of al-Hakim al-Shahid (the Martyr Judge), a prominent Hanafi scholar. It provides his full name and lineage, noting that he served as judge in Bukhara and later as minister to the ruler of Khurasan. There is a discrepancy in his death date: some sources say 344 AH, others 334 AH. He was martyred by Turks in Marw. The text describes his hadith memorization and his teachers and students. A tradition from al-Ashbah relates his own statement about his martyrdom and a story that attributes his fate to his abridgment of Imam Muhammad's works, which angered the Imam in a dream. Despite this, his two works, al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa, are considered foundational within the Hanafi school after the books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
الحاكم الشهيد (al-Hakim al-Shahid): Title meaning 'the Martyr Judge', referring to Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi al-Balkhi, a Hanafi scholar and judge.
الكافي (al-Kafi): One of al-Hakim al-Shahid's major works, a summary and abridgment of Hanafi fiqh.
المنتقى (al-Muntaqa): Another major work by al-Hakim al-Shahid, also a selection of rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the significance of al-Hakim al-Shahid's books al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa in the Hanafi school?
A) They are commentaries on the Qur'an
B) They are considered primary sources of hadith
C) They are foundational works after the books of Imam Muhammad
D) They were written by Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim al-Shahid's life reminds us that the texts of our school are a trust, and altering them without necessity can lead to spiritual and material harm.
