Who is al-Hasan in Hanafi Fiqh?
Biography of a Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i and explain why the unqualified name 'al-Hasan' in Hanafi fiqh works always refers to him rather than al-Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh books, 'al-Hasan' refers to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, not al-Hasan al-Basri.

The name 'al-Hasan' appears frequently in Hanafi fiqh texts, often without further qualification. This passage from a classical Hanafi primer on the rules of ifta' clarifies exactly which scholar is meant. Understanding this naming convention is essential for correctly attributing rulings and avoiding confusion between two famous scholars of the same name.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person
Read the opening line: 'Al-Hasan: He is Ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i al-Kufi, companion of Abu Hanifa.' Note his full name, lineage, and relationship to Abu Hanifa.
2
Extract key biographical traits
From the description, list his mental qualities (alert, intelligent, insightful) and his role as a judge. Note the anecdote about tawfiq leaving him when sitting to judge.
This anecdote illustrates the distinction between knowledge and judicial success.
3
Note his scholarly contributions
He was a memorizer of narrations from Abu Hanifa and wrote 12,000 hadith from Ibn Jurayj. This shows his role in transmitting hadith and fiqh.
4
Understand the naming convention
The final 'fa'ida' clarifies: in Hanafi books 'al-Hasan' unqualified means al-Hasan ibn Ziyad; in tafsir books it means al-Hasan al-Basri. Memorize this rule to avoid misattribution.
This is a critical parsing rule for reading Hanafi texts.
5
Apply the convention
When you encounter 'al-Hasan' in a Hanafi work, immediately identify it as al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. Test yourself with sample sentences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحسن : هو ابن زياد اللؤلؤى الكوفي، صاحب أبي حنيفة . كان يقظا، فطنا، فقيها ، نبيها ، وعن يحيى بن آدم : 'ما رأيت أفقه من الحسن بن زيادة ' . ولى القضاء بالكوفة بعد حفص بن غياث سنة ١٩٤هـ ثم استعفى، وكان محبا للسنة واتباعها، وكان يكسو مماليكه مما يكسو نفسه، وكان حافظاً للروايات عن أبي حنيفة، وكان إذا جلس ليحكم ذهب عنه التوفيق حتى سأل أصحابه عن الحكم في ذلك، فإذا قام عن مجلس القضاء عاد إلى ما كان عليه من الحفظ. فبعث إليه البكالى وقال : ' ويحك إنك لم توفق للقضاء فاستعف' . فاستعفى واستراح، وكان يقول : كتبت عن ابن جريج اثنى عشر ألف حديث كلها يحتاج إليها الفقهاء ' . عن الطحاوي : أن الحسن بن زياد والحسن ابن أبي مالك ماتا في سنة ٢٠٤هـ، وفي هذه السنة مات الشافعى بمصر . فائدة : الحسن إذا ذكر مطلقا في كتب أصحابنا فالمراد به الحسن بن زیاد اللؤلؤى' ، وإذا ذكر مطلقا في كتب التفسير فالمراد به الحسن البصرى'، كذا قال الإتقانى في غاية البيان حاشية الهداية نقلا عن شيخه برهان الدين الخريفعنى .
Al-Hasan: He is Ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i al-Kufi, companion of Abu Hanifa. He was alert, intelligent, a jurist, insightful. From Yahya ibn Adam: 'I have not seen anyone more juristic than al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.' He became judge in Kufa after Hafs ibn Ghiyath in 194 AH, then resigned. He loved the Sunna and following it. He would clothe his slaves with the same clothes he wore. He was a memorizer of narrations from Abu Hanifa. When he sat to judge, success (tawfiq) left him, so he would ask his companions for the ruling in that matter; when he rose from the judgment seat, his memory would return. So al-Bakali sent to him saying: 'Woe to you, you have not been given success in judging, so resign.' He resigned and found rest. He used to say: 'I wrote from Ibn Jurayj twelve thousand hadith, all of which the jurists need.' From al-Tahawi: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and al-Hasan ibn Abi Malik died in 204 AH, and in that year al-Shafi'i died in Egypt. Benefit: When 'al-Hasan' is mentioned absolutely in the books of our companions (the Hanafis), what is meant is al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i; when mentioned absolutely in books of tafsir, what is meant is al-Hasan al-Basri. Thus said al-Itqani in Ghayat al-Bayan, a gloss on al-Hidayah, quoting his teacher Burhan al-Din al-Kharif'ani.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, a prominent student of Abu Hanifa. It highlights his legal acumen, as praised by Yahya ibn Adam. He served as judge in Kufa but resigned due to a lack of divine success (tawfiq) in that role, an interesting anecdote about the distinction between knowledge and judicial capacity. He was known for his vast memorization of hadith, especially from Ibn Jurayj. His death year is given as 204 AH, same as al-Shafi'i. The passage ends with a valuable 'fa'ida' (benefit) clarifying the naming convention: in Hanafi fiqh books, the unqualified name 'al-Hasan' refers to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, while in tafsir books it refers to al-Hasan al-Basri. This is a crucial point for readers of Hanafi texts to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
الحسن (al-Hasan): The unqualified name 'al-Hasan' in Hanafi fiqh works refers specifically to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He was forced out by the ruler
B) He lost his memory when sitting to judge
C) He preferred teaching over judging

Key Takeaway
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad is a major Hanafi authority whose unqualified name 'al-Hasan' in Hanafi fiqh refers to him, not to al-Hasan al-Basri.

Al-Hakim al-Shahid: A Pillar of the Hanafi School
Biographical entry on al-Hakim al-Shahid, his death and works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key contributions of al-Hakim al-Shahid to the Hanafi madhhab and explain the significance of his works al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa in the mufti's hierarchy of sources.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim al-Shahid's works are foundational after Imam Muhammad's six books; his tragic death warns against altering scholarly heritage.

This passage introduces us to al-Hakim al-Shahid, a towering Hanafi scholar whose compilations al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa became essential references for later jurists. Understanding his biography helps the mufti appreciate the chain of authority and the weight these works carry in fatwa derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his historical context
Locate the scholar's name, death date, and place of death. Note that he was killed in 334 AH by the Turks in Marw.
This establishes the era and the political environment affecting scholars.
2
Trace his scholarly lineage
Identify his teachers (e.g., Abu Raja' Muhammad ibn Hamdawayh) and his prominent students (e.g., al-Hakim al-Naysaburi). This shows his connection to earlier and later authorities.
His students include the famous muhaddith al-Hakim al-Naysaburi, author of al-Mustadrak.
3
Analyze the story of his death
Read the account of his dream and the lesson it imparts. Reflect on the statement: 'This is the recompense of one who preferred this world over the Hereafter.'
The story underscores the importance of respecting the works of earlier imams and the dangers of altering them.
4
Assess the contribution of his works
Note that al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa are described as 'two foundations of the school after the books of Muhammad.' Understand their place in the Hanafi textual hierarchy.
These works are considered primary sources (usul) after the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأعلام الوارد ذكرهم في الشرح
قتل سنة ٣٣٤هـ ، وبه قال المصنف كما سيأتي . ودفن بـ "مرو" برأس مقبرة "سوركدان" ، كما في الجواهر . وسمع الحديث بمرو على أبي رجاء محمد بن حمدويه (وهو يروى عن أحمد بن حنبل وغيره) وسمع منه أئمة خراسان وحفاظها قاطبة منهم : أبو عبد الله الحاكم الحافظ صاحب المستدرك ، وكان يحفظ ستين ألفا من حديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم . وفى الأشباه نقلا عن تلقيح المحبوبي : أنه قال حين ابتلى بمحنة القتل بمرو من جهة الأتراك : "هذه جزاء من آثر الدنيا على الآخرة، والعالم متى أخفى علمه وترك حقه خيف عليه أن يمتحن بمايسوؤه . وقيل : كان سبب ذلك أنه لما رأى في كتب محمد مكررات وتطويلات خلسها وحذف مكررها فرأی محمد رحمه الله في منامه، فقال: لما فعلت هذا بكتبي؟ " فقال : "لأن فى الفقهاء كسالى فحذفت المكرر، وذكرت المقرر تسهيلا فغضب وقال : "قطعك الله كما قطعت كتبي " . فابتلى بالأتراك حتى جعلوه على رأس شجرتين فتقطع نصفين " . وكتابه "الكافي" و"المنتقى " أصلان من أصول المذهب بعد كتب محمد رحمه الله ، وهما يدلان على كمال فضله وتبحره في الفقه .
He was killed in the year 334 AH, and the author (al-musannif) said according to him as will come. He was buried in Marw at the head of the cemetery of Surkdan, as in al-Jawahir. He heard hadith in Marw from Abu Raja' Muhammad ibn Hamdawayh (who narrated from Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others), and from him heard the imams of Khorasan and all its memorizers, among them: Abu Abdullah al-Hakim al-Hafiz, author of al-Mustadrak, and he memorized sixty thousand hadiths of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. And in al-Ashbah quoting from Talqih al-Mahbubi: that he said when he was afflicted with the trial of being killed in Marw at the hands of the Turks: 'This is the recompense of one who preferred this world over the Hereafter; and when a scholar hides his knowledge and abandons his right, it is feared that he will be tested with what distresses him.' And it was said: the cause of that was that when he saw in the books of Muhammad repetitions and lengthy passages, he stole them and deleted their repetitions. Then he saw Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, in his dream, and he said: 'Why did you do this to my books?' He said: 'Because among the jurists are lazy ones, so I deleted the repetitions and mentioned the settled matters to make easy.' So he became angry and said: 'May Allah cut you as you cut my books.' So he was afflicted by the Turks until they placed him on top of two trees and he was cut in half.' And his book al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa are two foundations of the school after the books of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and they indicate the perfection of his virtue and his deep knowledge of fiqh.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of al-Hakim al-Shahid (Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi), a prominent Hanafi scholar who compiled al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa, two essential works of the madhhab after the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage notes his death in 334 AH at the hands of the Turks, and recounts a story from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir about why he was killed: he abridged the books of Imam Muhammad, removing repetitions, and was punished for it in a dream. His works are considered foundational for the Hanafi school after the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
المصنف (al-musannif): In this context, refers to the author of the original matn 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' (Ibn Kamal Pasha).
الكافي (al-Kafi): One of al-Hakim al-Shahid's major works, a foundational text in the Hanafi school.
المنتقى (al-Muntaqa): Another major work by al-Hakim al-Shahid, also considered a foundational source after Imam Muhammad's books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim al-Shahid's al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa are the next tier of authority after Imam Muhammad's six books, forming a crucial part of the Hanafi textual hierarchy.

The Authority of al-Khassaf in Hanafi Fara'id
Biographical entry on al-Khassaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Khassaf's specialization and explain why his opinion is authoritative in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Al-Khassaf's expertise in inheritance made his rulings authoritative; his nickname reflects self-reliance.

This lesson introduces Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Khassaf, a prominent Hanafi jurist renowned for his mastery of inheritance law (fara'id). The passage from the text highlights his nickname, his death date, and a key ruling by Qadikhan affirming the permissibility of following him in prayer. Understanding his biography helps appreciate the weight of his contributions to Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person
Read the name and lineage: Ahmad ibn 'Umar (or 'Amr). Note the difference in vowelization but both are accepted.
The text notes the variant readings of his father's name.
2
Note his Specialization
He is described as 'faradiyyan' (inheritance expert) and 'muhasiban' (calculator). This shows his deep knowledge in fara'id.
Fara'id requires both legal and arithmetical skills.
3
Understand the Nickname
Al-Khassaf means 'the tanner' or 'the one who works with leather' – he earned his living by manual labor, indicating his humility and self-sufficiency.
The nickname derives from his craft.
4
Recognize his Authority
Qadikhan states that it is permissible to follow al-Khassaf in prayer, which implies his high rank as a knowledgeable imam.
This indicates his reliability and scholarly stature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٣ الخصاف : هو أحمد بن عمر (بالضم على ما قاله الكفوى) أو عمرو بالفتح كما في سير النبلاء للذهبي كان ،فرضيا، محاسباً، عارفاً بمذهب أبي حنيفة، ولقب بالخصاف ؛ لأنه كان يأكل من صنعته بيده مات سنة ٢٦١هـ، وقد قارب الثمانين . قال الشامي قال قاضيخان والخصاف كان كبيراً في العلم يجوز الاقتداء به .
33 - al-Khassaf: He is Ahmad ibn 'Umar (with damma according to al-Kafawi) or 'Amr with fatha as in Siyar al-Nubala' by al-Dhahabi. He was a faradi (inheritance expert), a calculator, well-versed in the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. He was nicknamed al-Khassaf because he would eat from his own handiwork. He died in the year 261 AH, nearing eighty. Al-Shami said: Qadikhan said: al-Khassaf was great in knowledge; it is permissible to follow him (in prayer).
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This brief biography introduces Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Khassaf, a renowned Hanafi jurist specializing in inheritance law (fara'id) and mathematics. His nickname 'al-Khassaf' comes from his practice of earning a living by his own handiwork. The passage also notes a ruling from Qadikhan that it is permissible to follow al-Khassaf in prayer, indicating his high stature as a scholar.

Key Terms
الخصاف (al-Khassaf): A Hanafi jurist known for expertise in inheritance law; his name is derived from his manual labor.
فرضيا (faradiyyan): Expert in inheritance law (fara'id).
محاسبا (muhasiban): A calculator, skilled in arithmetic needed for inheritance computations.

Al-Dhahabi: The Hadith Scholar and His Legacy
Biographical entry on al-Dhahabi with list of works and death date dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key contributions of al-Dhahabi and evaluate the evidence for his death date using scholarly criteria.

Core Idea
Al-Dhahabi's biographical works are indispensable for Hanafi hadith criticism despite his Shafi'i/Hanbali affiliation.

Al-Dhahabi is a towering figure in hadith and history, whose works like Mizan al-I'tidal and Siyar al-Nubala' are essential tools for rijal criticism across all madhhabs. This lesson covers his life, major works, and a scholarly dispute over his death date that tests our ability to weigh historical evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Note al-Dhahabi's full name, birth year (673 AH), key teachers (e.g., Ibn al-Zamalkani), and areas of mastery (qira'at, hadith, rijal, history).
His kunya is Shams al-Din; he is known as al-Dhahabi.
2
Catalog his major works
List the works mentioned: Mizan al-I'tidal, Siyar al-Nubala', al-'Ibar, al-Kashif, and many concise versions (Mukhtasarat) of other scholars' compilations.
These works are central for narrator criticism and historical research.
3
Note his madhhab and creed
The passage states he was Shafi'i in fiqh and Hanbali in creed, clarifying a common misconception that he was Hanafi.
His works are accepted across madhhabs due to his objectivity.
4
Examine the death date controversy
The text gives 740 AH as the accepted date (from Ibn Shahba's Tabaqat), but al-Kashf records 848 AH. Note the evidence: al-Dhahabi finished Majma' al-Zawa'id in 720 AH, making 848 impossible.
Shaykh Muhammad Zakariyya provides critical analysis.
5
Evaluate the resolution
The author sides with 740 AH, citing multiple indications (qara'in). Recognize how internal evidence from an author's own works can resolve dating disputes.
This showcases the method of historical criticism (naqd).

34 - al-Dhahabi: He is the hafiz Shams al-Din Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Uthman al-Turkmani, al-Dimashqi, al-Dhahabi. He was born in Rabi' al-Akhir 673 AH, and heard from many people, over a thousand, and studied fiqh with Kamal al-Din ibn al-Zamalkani and others. He read and mastered the qira'at, and mastered hadith, criticism of narrators, and history. Al-Subki said of him: 'The hadith scholar of the age, the seal of the memorizers, the imam of the age in memory and mastery.' He died in 740 AH, as in Tabaqat of Ibn Shahba. Among his many works are Mizan al-I'tidal, Siyar al-Nubala', al-'Ibar fi Akhbar man Ghabar, al-Kashif (a summary of Tahdhib al-Kamal). He has many other works: al-Mughni fi Asma' al-Rijal, Mukhtasar Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Mukhtasar Atraf al-Mizzi, Tabaqat al-Huffaz, Tabaqat al-Qurra', Tajrid al-Sahaba, Mukhtasar Mustadrak al-Hakim, Mukhtasar Tarikh Naysabur al-Hakim, Mukhtasar al-Mu'jam al-Kabir wa al-Saghir by al-Tabrani, and others. He was Shafi'i in madhhab and Hanbali in creed. The author of Madinat al-'Ilm mentioned him, as in al-Ta'liqat al-Sunniyya. In al-Kashf, when mentioning al-Kashif by al-Dhahabi, it says he died in 848 AH, but on its margin our shaykh Muhammad Zakariyya, author of al-Awjaz, wrote: 'I say: the apparent is contrary; because he finished composing Majma' al-Zawa'id in 720 AH, so the apparent is seven hundred [i.e., 740 AH]. And there are many indications.' I say: rather it is correct; because the author of al-Kashf mentioned it thus when mentioning Mizan al-I'tidal, Siyar al-Nubala', and al-'Ibar fi Akhbar...

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of al-Dhahabi, a towering figure in hadith and history. Though he was Shafi'i in fiqh and Hanbali in creed, his biographical works are essential for all Islamic scholars. The text also records a debate about his death date: the widely accepted date is 740 AH, but some sources claim 848 AH. The author of al-Kashf supports the later date, but Shaykh Muhammad Zakariyya argues against it using evidence from al-Dhahabi's own works. The passage ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الذهبي (al-Dhahabi): Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Dhahabi, a renowned hadith scholar and historian despite being non-Hanafi in madhhab.

Biography of al-Khassaf: Hanafi Fara'id Expert
Biographical entry for a Hanafi jurist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of al-Khassaf and explain the significance of his nickname and scholarly endorsement in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Khassaf's expertise in fara’id and his nickname 'al-Khassaf' reflect his manual craft, not a scholarly title.

This lesson introduces Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Khassaf, a Hanafi jurist renowned for his mastery of inheritance law (fara’id). The text clarifies a dispute over his father’s name and explains the origin of his unique nickname. Understanding his biography helps us appreciate the chain of scholarly authority in the Hanafi madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and naming variants
Note that the father's name is given as 'Umar (with dammah) or 'Amr (with fath). Both are considered valid.
Al-Kafawi prefers 'Umar, while al-Dhahabi uses 'Amr in Siyar al-Nubala'.
2
Determine his specialization
The text explicitly calls him 'fardiyan', an expert in fara'id (inheritance), and also mentions he was an accountant and knowledgeable in the Hanafi madhhab.
His specialization directly aligns with the subject of fara'id, a core area of Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the nickname 'al-Khassaf'
The nickname comes from his manual labor (tanning or leatherwork); he earned his livelihood from his craft. This is a notable attribute for a scholar.
It shows he was self-sufficient and humble, a model for later scholars.
4
Note his death and age
He died in 261 AH at nearly 80 years old. This places him in the early 3rd century AH, among the earlier Hanafi authorities.
His lifespan overlaps with major Hanafi figures.
5
Analyze the scholarly endorsement
Qadi Khan, quoted by al-Shami, states that al-Khassaf was great in knowledge and it is permissible to follow him (fi al-iftā'). This confirms his reliability as a mufti.
This endorsement is important for the chain of iftā' in the Hanafi school.

This is a biographical entry on Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Khassaf, a prominent Hanafi jurist. He was known for his expertise in fara'id (inheritance law) and accounting, and fully versed in the Hanafi madhhab. His nickname 'al-Khassaf' derives from his manual labor (tanning or leatherwork), as he earned his livelihood by his own hands. He died in 261 AH at about 80 years of age. The text quotes Qadi Khan through al-Shami, attesting to his high scholarly station and the permissibility of following him in legal matters.

Biography of al-Dhahabi: Scholar of Hadith and History
Biographical entry with death year correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of al-Dhahabi (name, birth, death, madhhab, major works) and explain the scholarly resolution of the dispute over his death year.

Core Idea
Al-Dhahabi's correct death year is 740 AH (not 848 AH) as evidenced by his completion of Mujma' al-Zawa'id in 720 AH.

This lesson presents the biography of Shams al-Din al-Dhahabi, one of the most authoritative hadith critics and historians in Islamic scholarship. Though he was Shafi'i in fiqh, his works are indispensable for muftis and scholars of jarh wa ta'dil. The passage also highlights a common error regarding his death date and resolves it through textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Name and Lineage
Identify al-Dhahabi's full name: Shams al-Din Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Uthman al-Turkmani al-Dimashqi al-Dhahabi. Note his birth in 673 AH in Rabi' al-Akhir.
His nisba 'al-Dhahabi' (the goldsmith) may come from his father's profession.
2
Teachers and Learning
He heard from over a thousand teachers, studied fiqh under Kamal al-Din ibn al-Zamalkani, and mastered Qira'at, Hadith, and history.
This breadth of learning made him a comprehensive scholar.
3
Major Works
List his key works: Mizan al-I'tidal, Siyar al-Nubala', al-'Ibar, al-Kashif, al-Mughni, and numerous abridgments of major hadith collections.
Mizan al-I'tidal is a standard reference for narrator criticism.
4
Madhhab and Creed
He was Shafi'i in fiqh and Hanbali in 'aqida. This is important because his theological leanings influenced his criticisms in works like Mizan.
His Hanbali 'aqida means he adhered to the Athari creed.
5
Death Year Dispute
Some sources state 848 AH, but the correct date is 740 AH. The evidence: he completed Mujma' al-Zawa'id in 720 AH, so a death in 848 is impossible. Also, al-Kashf lists his works and gives 740 AH.
The error likely stems from misreading numerals (740 vs 848).
6
Zamzam Benefit Story
A later scholar (al-Hafiz) drank Zamzam and prayed for memory like al-Dhahabi's. His memory improved in texts and defects but not in narrators, showing al-Dhahabi's unmatched expertise in rijal.
This story illustrates the high regard for al-Dhahabi's mastery.

34. Al-Dhahabi: He is the Hafiz Shams al-Din Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Uthman al-Turkmani, al-Dimashqi, al-Dhahabi. He was born in Rabi' al-Akhir 673 AH, and heard from many people, over a thousand, and studied fiqh from Kamal al-Din ibn al-Zamalkani and others, and read the various Qira'at and mastered them, and mastered the science of Hadith, criticism of narrators, and history. Al-Subki said of him: 'The Muhaddith of the age, the seal of the Hufaz, the Imam of the age in memorization and mastery.' He died in 740 AH, as in Tabaqat of Ibn Shahba. Among his many works: Mizan al-I'tidal, Siyar al-Nubala', al-'Ibar fi Akhbar man Ghabar, and al-Kashif, an abridgment of Tahdhib al-Kamal. He also authored many others: al-Mughni fi Asma' al-Rijal, Mukhtasar Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Mukhtasar Atraf al-Muzani, Tabaqat al-Huffaz, Tabaqat al-Qurra', Tajrid al-Sahaba, Mukhtasar Mustadrak al-Hakim, Mukhtasar Tarikh Naysabur li'l-Hakim, Mukhtasar al-Mu'jam al-Kabir wa al-Saghir li'l-Tabarani, and others. He was Shafi'i in madhhab and Hanbali in creed, as mentioned by the author of Madinat al-'Ulum, and similarly in al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyya. In al-Kashf, when mentioning al-Kashif of al-Dhahabi, it is said he died in 848 AH, but on its margin our Shaykh Muhammad Zakariyya, author of al-Awjaz, wrote: 'I say: The apparent evidence rejects it, because he completed Mujma' al-Zawa'id in 720 AH, so the date there is seven hundred.' There are many indications. I say: Rather the correct is 740 AH, because the author of al-Kashf mentioned it that way when listing Mizan al-I'tidal, Siyar al-Nubala', al-'Ibar, al-Kamal fi Ma'rifat al-Rijal, etc. Benefit: In Fayd al-Bazi, it is mentioned that al-Hafiz (al-Dhahabi) drank Zamzam during his Hajj and prayed that his memory would be blessed like al-Dhahabi's. Then, when he visited the House a second time, he saw that his memory had surpassed him. Then Shaykh al-Anwar said: 'The purpose of al-Hafiz was an increase in memory concerning texts and defects, but concerning narrators I do not see that he surpassed him.'
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This is a detailed biography of the celebrated scholar al-Dhahabi. The text provides his full lineage, birth in 673 AH, his vast learning, and his mastery of hadith, rijal, and history. It notes that he was Shafi'i in fiqh but Hanbali in creed. His many seminal works are listed. A critical note discusses confusion over his death year: some sources say 848 AH, but the correct date is 740 AH, as argued by Shaykh Muhammad Zakariyya. The benefit (fa'idah) recounts a story where a later scholar, after drinking Zamzam, prayed for excellence in hadith memorization and later found his memory improved, though not surpassing al-Dhahabi's knowledge of narrators.

Key Terms
الذهبي (al-Dhahabi): Shams al-Din Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad, the renowned hadith critic and historian, Shafi'i in fiqh and Hanbali in 'aqida.
الحافظ (al-hafiz): A title for a master of Hadith who has memorized a vast number of narrations and their chains.

Al-Razi al-Jassas: Biography and Scholarly Rank
Biographical entry with name clarification and rank dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas as a major Hanafi authority, clarify the confusion about his name and death date, and evaluate the debate about his level of ijtihad.

Core Idea
Al-Razi and al-Jassas are one scholar; his rank as mujtahid is defended despite some later classifications.

In the Hanafi tradition, knowing the biographies of key scholars is essential for accurate attribution of rulings. This lesson introduces you to Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas, a towering figure often referenced in fiqh works. We will resolve common confusions about his name and death date, and examine a dispute about whether he was a mujtahid or merely a sahib takhrij.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and nisbah
Read the first line and note the full name: Ahmad ibn 'Ali Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas. Understand that 'al-Razi' refers to his origin from Rayy, and 'al-Jassas' is a nisbah to working with plaster (jass).
2
Determine the correct death year
The text gives two reported years: 370 AH (7 Dhu al-Hijjah) and 315 AH. The preferred opinion is 370 AH, as supported by al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah and the biographical works cited.
The discrepancy is resolved by preferring the later date from more reliable sources.
3
Resolve the name confusion
Some scholars mistakenly think 'al-Razi' and 'al-Jassas' are two different people. The text explicitly states they are the same person, and the author of al-Qamus made an error in his Tabaqat by treating them separately.
This confusion arose because different authors used one or the other nisbah.
4
Analyze the debate on ijtihad rank
The author of al-Qamus placed him among the ashab al-takhrij (those who derive rulings but are not independent mujtahids). Others object, arguing that his works and his influence on later mujtahids (like Shams al-A'immah) show he was himself a mujtahid.
This debate affects how his rulings are weighted in the madhhab hierarchy.
5
Note the additional benefit on al-Tahawi and al-Jassas
The text ends with a remark by al-Saffar that al-Tahawi was rarely mistaken, while al-Jassas was more prone to error. This highlights the importance of knowing the reliability of early authorities.
Such evaluations help muftis in preferring one narration over another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٥ الرازي : هو أحمد بن على أبو بكر الرازي الجصاص، كان إمام الحنفية في عصره مات سابع ذى الحجة سنة ٣٧٠هـ ، وقيل : سنة ٣١٥هـ. وكان مولده ببغداد سنة ٣٠٥ هـ. و الجصاص نسبة إلى العمل بالجص. وفى طبقات القارى : أحمد ابن على أبو بكر الرازي الإمام الكبير الشان المعروف بالجصاص وهو لقب له، وذكره بعض الأصحاب بلفظ الرازي، وبعضهم بلفظ الجصاص وهما واحد) خلافًا لمن توهم أنهما اثنان كما صرح به صاحب القاموس في طبقاته للحنفية. وقد جعله من أصحاب التخريج من المقلدين الذين لا يقدرون على الاجتهاد أصلا، وتعقب بعض الفضلاء : بأنه ظلم في حقه، وتنزيل له عن مجله، ومن تتبع تصانيفه والأقوال المنقولة عنه، علم أن الذين عدهم من المجتهدين كشمس الأئمة وغيره كلهم عيال عليه فهو أحق بأن يجعل من المجتهدين في المذهب. وفى الجواهر المضيئة وهو من جماعة الكرخي". وتمام ترجمته في طبقات التميمي، وذكر أن وفاته سنة ٣٧٠هـ عن خمس وستين سنة، وستله في تراجم العلامة قاسم. ثم اعلم أن صاحب الكشف يسميه تارة أحمد بن على، وتارة محمد بن على، وتارة محمد بن أحمد، والصواب هو الأول. فائدة : قال الصفار : كثيراً ما جربنا الطحاوى فلم نجده غالطًا، وكثيراً ما جربنا الخصاص فوجدناه غالطاً. كدا في حاشية الدر المختار للطحطاوي : (٥١٨/١).
35. Al-Razi: He is Ahmad ibn 'Ali Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas. He was the imam of the Hanafis in his time. He died on the 7th of Dhu al-Hijjah 370 AH, and it is also said 315 AH. He was born in Baghdad in 305 AH. 'Al-Jassas' is a nisbah to working with plaster (jass). In Tabaqat al-Qari: 'Ahmad ibn 'Ali Abu Bakr al-Razi, the great imam of high standing, known as al-Jassas, and it is a nickname for him. Some scholars mention him as al-Razi and some as al-Jassas, and they are the same person,' contrary to those who mistakenly think they are two, as stated by the author of al-Qamus in his Tabaqat for the Hanafis. He (al-Qamus) placed him among the ashab al-takhrij (deducers) from the muqallids who are not capable of ijtihad at all. But some virtuous scholars objected, saying that this is an injustice to him and a downgrading of his rank. Whoever examines his works and the transmitted opinions knows that those whom he counted among the mujtahids, such as Shams al-A'immah and others, are all dependent on him; he is more deserving to be counted among the mujtahids in the madhhab. In al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah: 'He is from the group of al-Karkhi.' His complete biography is in Tabaqat al-Tamimi, and it mentions that his death was in 370 AH at the age of sixty-five. And his biography is also in Tarajim al-'Allamah Qasim. Know that the author of al-Kashf calls him sometimes Ahmad ibn 'Ali, sometimes Muhammad ibn 'Ali, and sometimes Muhammad ibn Ahmad. The correct is the first. Benefit: Al-Saffar said: 'We often tested al-Tahawi and never found him mistaken, and we often tested al-Khassaf and found him mistaken.' As in Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar for al-Tahawi (1/518).
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This entry covers the biography of Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas, a leading Hanafi faqih from Baghdad. It clarifies that his nisbah 'al-Jassas' refers to working with plaster. The text resolves the common confusion that al-Razi and al-Jassas are two different persons; they are the same. There is a debate about his level: some consider him merely a 'sahib takhrij' (a deducer) not a mujtahid, but others defend his ijtihad, noting that later authoritative scholars like Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani relied on him. The text also notes discrepancies in his name in the works of Kashf al-Zunun, and affirms the correct name is Ahmad ibn 'Ali. A final benefit (fa'idah) compares al-Tahawi and al-Jassas: al-Tahawi was rarely mistaken, whereas al-Jassas was sometimes found in error.

Key Terms
الرازي الجصاص (al-Razi al-Jassas): Ahmad ibn 'Ali Abu Bakr, the great Hanafi jurist and Imam of his era, known both as al-Razi and al-Jassas.
أصحاب التخريج (ashab al-takhrij): Jurists who can derive rulings from the principles of the madhhab but are not independent mujtahids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 315 AH
B) 370 AH
C) 261 AH
D) 740 AH

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas is a major Hanafi jurist; his correct name is Ahmad ibn 'Ali, and his death year is 370 AH, and he is best considered a mujtahid in the madhhab.

Life and Works of Khayr al-Din al-Ramli
Biographical entry on a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Khayr al-Din al-Ramli and summarize his contributions to Hanafi fatwa literature.

Core Idea
Al-Ramli's al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya is an essential reference for later Hanafi muftis.

This lesson introduces Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, a towering figure of the 11th century AH whose fatwa collection has guided Hanafi jurists for centuries. Understanding his training, teachers, and works helps you appreciate the chain of authority in Hanafi ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify his full name and lineage
Read the opening line of the biography to extract his full genealogy and attributions.
Note multiple nisbas: al-Ayyubi, al-Ulaymi, al-Faruqi, al-Ramli.
2
List his scholarly disciplines
The text lists his expertise: tafsir, hadith, fiqh, etc. Count them.
He was a master of many fields – a polymath.
3
Record his teachers and students
Identify the two teachers named: Siraj al-Din al-Hanuni and Ahmad ibn Muhammad Amin al-Din.
His teachers link him to earlier authority.
4
Note his birth and death dates
Born 993 AH, died 1081 AH. This places him in the Ottoman period.
Remember: 993-1081 AH.
5
Catalog his major works
List the works mentioned: al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya, glosses on multiple texts, poetry.
His fatwa collection is the most important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرملي : هو خير الدين بن أحمد بن نور الدين على بن زين الدين الأيوبي (نسبة إلى بعض أجداده)، العليمي بالضم نسبة إلى سيدى على بن عليم، الولى المشهور) الفاروقي (نسبة إلى الفاروق عمر بن خطاب رضی الله عنه الرملي، إمام ،مفسر ،محدث ،فقیه ،لغوی ،صوفی ،نحوی ،بیانی، عروضی، شیخ الحنفية في عصره، أخذ عن سراح الدين الحانوني صاحب الفتاوى المشهورة، وأحمد بن محمد أمين الدين بن عبد العال، ودرس ببلده وبمصر، ولد سنة ٩٩٣هـ، وتوفى ببلده الرملة سنة ١٠٨١هـ. ومن تصانيفه : الفتاوى المعروفة بـ الخيرية" ، وحواشى على المنح ، وعلى شرح الكنز للعيني، وعلى الأشباه والنظائر، وعلى البحر الرائق، وعلى الزيلعي، وعلى جامع الفصولين ورسائل و دیوان شعر مرتب على حروف المعجم وغير ذلك وأطال الأمير المحبى الكلام في ذكر مناقبه وأحواله وبيان مشايخه وتلامذته . فليراجع
Al-Ramli: He is Khayr al-Din ibn Ahmad ibn Nur al-Din Ali ibn Zayn al-Din al-Ayyubi (attributed to some of his ancestors), al-Ulaymi (with a damma, attributed to Sayyidi Ali ibn Ulaym), the famous saint, al-Faruqi (attributed to al-Faruq Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him), al-Ramli. He was an imam, exegete, hadith scholar, jurist, linguist, Sufi, grammarian, rhetorician, prosodist, and the shaykh of the Hanafis in his time. He studied under Siraj al-Din al-Hanuni, author of the famous fatawa, and Ahmad ibn Muhammad Amin al-Din ibn Abd al-Aal. He taught in his town and in Egypt. He was born in 993 AH and died in his town of al-Ramla in 1081 AH. Among his works are: the fatawa known as al-Khayriyya, glosses on al-Manh, on Sharh al-Kanz by al-Ayni, on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, on al-Bahr al-Raiq, on al-Zaylai, on Jami al-Fusulayn, letters, and a diwan of poetry arranged alphabetically, and others. Al-Amir al-Muhibbi spoke at length about his virtues, his states, his teachers, and his students. Let him be consulted.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This is a biographical entry on Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, a prominent Hanafi scholar. His full lineage shows noble descent. He was a master of many sciences: tafsir, hadith, fiqh, linguistics, Sufism, grammar, rhetoric, and prosody. He studied under notable scholars including Siraj al-Din al-Hanuni, author of famous fatawa. His birth and death dates are given (993-1081 AH). His most famous work is the fatwa collection al-Khayriyya. He also wrote glosses on several important Hanafi texts such as al-Manh, Sharh al-Kanz by al-Ayni, al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, al-Bahr al-Raiq, and others. He also composed poetry. The text recommends consulting al-Muhibbi's biography for more details.

Key Terms
الرملي (al-Ramli): The nisba referring to Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, a 11th-century Hanafi scholar from al-Ramla.
الفتاوى الخيرية (al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya): The famous fatwa collection of al-Ramli, a key reference for later Hanafi muftis.
شيخ الحنفية (Shaykh al-Hanafiyya): Title meaning the leading authority of the Hanafi school in a given era.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Imam Zufar: Abu Hanifa's Foremost Qiyas Expert
Biographical entry on Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key facts about Imam Zufar's life and rank among Abu Hanifa's companions, and explain why his mastery of qiyas is significant for Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
Zufar was Abu Hanifa's foremost qiyas expert, a respected imam, and a pivotal figure in early Hanafi legal reasoning.

In the Hanafi madhhab, certain figures stand out not only as students but as exemplars of specific legal methods. Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl was one such figure—renowned by Abu Hanifa himself as the best in qiyas (analogical reasoning). This biographical lesson introduces you to his life, his high rank, and his legacy, which continues to inform the mufti's approach today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his lineage
Locate the name, full lineage, and birthplace. Zufar is Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl al-Basri. Note his origin and connection to Basra.
2
Extract Abu Hanifa's assessment
Find the direct quote from Abu Hanifa: 'Huwa aqyas ashabi' (He is the best of my companions in qiyas). Memorize this—it is the single most important statement about Zufar.
Qiyas is a core tool for a mufti; Zufar's excellence in it sets a benchmark.
3
Understand his rank in the study circle
Note that Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said Zufar was given precedence in the Imam's circle. This indicates his privilege and responsibility.
Precedence reflects seniority and trust.
4
Analyze the wedding sermon anecdote
Abu Hanifa, in his sermon at Zufar's wedding, declared Zufar 'an imam among the imams of the Muslims.' This publicly affirms Zufar's scholarly authority.
Not just a private compliment, but a public endorsement.
5
Interpret the debate with Abu Yusuf
Dawud al-Ta'i reports that Zufar was eloquent and confident in debate, while Abu Yusuf became flustered. Zufar's rhetorical question—'Where are you fleeing? These are open doors'—shows his mastery of multiple argumentative paths.
This demonstrates the breadth of his qiyas: many possible analogies exist, and a skilled jurist can navigate them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زفر : هو زفر بن الهذيل بن قيس البصري. كان أبو حنيفة يبجله ويعظمه ويقول : هو أقيس أصحابي. وقال الحسن بن زياد "إن المقدم في مجلس الإمام كان زفر " . عن سليمان العطار قال : "تزوج زفر ودعى إلى عرسه الإمام، فالتمس منه أن يخطب فقال في خطبته: "هذا زفر إمام من أئمة المسلمين " . وعلم من إعلامهم في شرفه وحسبه ونسبه . قال أبو نعيم : كان ثقة مأمونا، دخل البصرة في ميراث أخيه، فتشبت به أهل البصرة فمنعوه الخروج منها ، ومات بها سنة ١٥٨هـ، ومولده سنة عشر بعد المائة " . وعن داود الطائي قال : كان أبو يوسف وزفر يتناظران في الفقه وكان زفر جيد اللسان، وكان أبو يوسف يضطرب فى مناظرته. فربما سمعت زفر يقول له : أين تفر، هذه أبواب مفتحة خذ أيها شئت" .
Zufar: He is Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl ibn Qays al-Basri. Abu Hanifa used to honor and revere him and said: 'He is the best of my companions in qiyas.' Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: 'The one who was given precedence in the circle of the Imam was Zufar.' From Sulayman al-Attar: 'Zufar got married and invited the Imam to his wedding, and asked him to deliver a sermon. He said in his sermon: 'This Zufar is an imam among the imams of the Muslims.' And it is known from their signs of his honor, lineage, and nobility. Abu Nuaym said: 'He was trustworthy and reliable. He entered Basra for the inheritance of his brother, and the people of Basra clung to him and prevented him from leaving. He died there in 158 AH, and his birth was in 110 AH.' From Dawud al-Ta'i: 'Abu Yusuf and Zufar used to debate in fiqh, and Zufar was well-spoken, while Abu Yusuf would become flustered in his debate. Sometimes you would hear Zufar say to him: 'Where are you fleeing? These are open doors; take whichever you wish.'
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This is a biographical entry on Zufar al-Basri, one of the foremost students of Abu Hanifa. The text emphasizes his high rank: Abu Hanifa himself praised his ability in qiyas (analogical reasoning), calling him 'the best of my companions in qiyas.' He was given precedence in Abu Hanifa's study circle. An anecdote from his wedding shows the esteem Abu Hanifa had for him, publicly declaring him an imam. Abu Nuaym confirms his trustworthiness. He died in Basra in 158 AH. A debate story with Abu Yusuf illustrates Zufar's eloquence and confidence in argumentation.

Key Terms
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, one of the foremost students of Abu Hanifa, known for his expertise in qiyas.
أقيس أصحابي (aqyas ashabi): The best of my companions in qiyas (analogical reasoning).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is the most knowledgeable in hadith
B) He is the best of my companions in qiyas
C) He is the best of my companions in fatwa
D) He is the most ascetic of my companions

Key Takeaway
Imam Zufar was Abu Hanifa's premier qiyas expert, and his life and method provide a model for muftis in performing rigorous analogical reasoning.

Biography of Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki
Biographical entry on a Shafi'i scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki and explain why his fatwa collection is relevant to Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki was a leading Shafi'i mujtahid whose fatwa collection is frequently referenced in later Hanafi works.

Even in a Hanafi usul work like Rasm al-Mufti, we encounter biographical entries on scholars from other madhhabs. Why? Because a mufti must know the authorities behind the rulings he may encounter or need to reference. Imam al-Subki's fatwas, compiled by his son, became a standard source for later jurists across schools.

Guided Path
1
Locate the basic identity of the scholar
Identify his full name, lineage, madhhab, birth and death dates. Note the differences between the two death years given.
Al-Subki is Shafi'i, not Hanafi, yet he appears in a Hanafi work.
2
Identify his teachers and fields of study
List the subjects he studied and under whom: fiqh under Ibn al-Rifa, hadith under al-Sharaf al-Dimyati, grammar under Abu Hayyan.
This shows his comprehensive training.
3
Understand his scholarly rank
Read the quote from al-Salah al-Saghdhi comparing him to al-Ghazali and Sufyan al-Thawri. Understand that he was considered a mujtahid by al-Suyuti.
His rank as mujtahid justifies the wide reference to his fatwas.
4
Note his works and fatwa collection
He authored over sixty works. His fatwas were collected by his son Taj al-Din in three volumes, known as Fatawa al-Subki.
This collection is a primary source for Shafi'i fatwa and is also used by Hanafi muftis for comparison.
5
Connect to Hanafi fatwa practice
Consider why a Hanafi mufti would cite a Shafi'i fatwa: when no clear Hanafi text exists (mas'alah sakt anha), or for illustration of ikhtilaf.
This shows the importance of knowing key figures from other madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمام السبكى : هو تقى الدين أبو الحسن علی بن عبد الكافي بن تمام ابن حماد السبكي الشافعي ولد بسبك في صفر سنة ٦٨٣هـ . وتفقه بابن الرفعة وأخذ الحديث عن الشرف الدمياطي، والنحو عن أبي حيان، وانتهت إليه رياسة أهل العلم بمصر. قال الصلاح الصغدى: "الناس يقولون : ما جاء بعد الغزالي مثله، وعندى أنهم يظلمونه وما هو عندي إلا مثل سفيان الثورى" . وله تصانيف جليلة تزيد على الستين ذكرها السيوطي في "حسن المحاضرة". وعده من المجتهدين وأرخ وفاته سنة ٧٥٦هـ، كذا في التعليقات السنية لمولانا عبد الحي وفتاواه المذكورة في المتن مشهورة بفتاوى السبكي، جمعها ولده تاج الدين عبد الوهاب في ثلاث مجلدات، وتوفى سنة إحدى وسبعين وسبعمائة كذا فى الكشف .
Imam al-Subki: He is Taqi al-Din Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abd al-Kafi ibn Tammam ibn Hammad al-Subki al-Shafi'i. He was born in Subk in Safar in the year 683 AH. He studied fiqh under Ibn al-Rifa, took hadith from al-Sharaf al-Dimyati, and grammar from Abu Hayyan. The leadership of the people of knowledge in Egypt culminated in him. Al-Salah al-Saghdhi said: 'People say: No one like al-Ghazali has come after him, but I think they are unjust to him, and he is in my view only like Sufyan al-Thawri.' He has many works, over sixty, mentioned by al-Suyuti in Husn al-Muhadara. He counted him among the mujtahids and recorded his death in 756 AH. That is in al-Taliqat al-Sunniyya by Mawlana Abd al-Hayy. His fatawa mentioned in the text are famous as Fatawa al-Subki, collected by his son Taj al-Din Abd al-Wahhab in three volumes. He died in 771 AH according to al-Kashf.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This is a biographical entry on Taqi al-Din al-Subki, a major Shafi'i scholar. He was born in 683 AH and died in either 756 AH or 771 AH according to different sources. He studied under prominent teachers and became the head of the scholarly community in Egypt. The text quotes al-Salah al-Saghdhi praising him even above al-Ghazali, likening him to Sufyan al-Thawri. His works number over sixty. His fatwas were collected by his son in three volumes. Al-Suyuti considered him a mujtahid.

Key Terms
السبكي (al-Subki): Taqi al-Din al-Subki, a Shafi'i scholar and mujtahid, author of Fatawa al-Subki.
فتاوى السبكي (Fatawa al-Subki): Collection of al-Subki's fatwas in three volumes by his son.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A scholar qualified to derive rulings directly from sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Ibn al-Rifa

D) Al-Salah al-Saghdhi

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Subki's biography demonstrates that a mufti must know the key figures of other schools because their fatwas can be valuable references when the Hanafi school lacks explicit rulings.

Biography of Imam Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani
Biographical entry on Imam al-Sha'rani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Imam al-Sha'rani and explain the significance of differing accounts of his death year in Islamic biographical literature.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sha'rani, a prolific Sufi scholar and author, left a rich legacy, but historians disagree on his exact year of death.

This lesson introduces you to Imam Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, a towering figure in Sufi literature and Islamic scholarship. Born in the 10th century AH, he authored numerous works that remain influential. However, like many pre-modern figures, his death date is recorded differently by various sources. Understanding why such discrepancies occur is an important skill in Islamic biographical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person
Who is al-Sha'rani? Look at his full name: Shaykh Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ahmad al-Sha'rani. Note his title 'Imam' and his reputation as a prolific author.
Al-Sha'rani is a famous Sufi scholar from Egypt.
2
List his works mentioned
The passage mentions several of his works: al-Yawaqit, al-Kibrit al-Ahmar, al-Mizan, Lawaqih al-Anwar fi Tabaqat al-Sada al-Akhyar, Lawaqih al-Anwar al-Qudsiyya, and Baruq al-Khawatif (though the last is cut off).
He is known for many other works on Sufism and fiqh.
3
Examine the death dates
The author of al-Kashf reports his death in 976 AH when mentioning al-Yawaqit. Other sources (al-Kibrit al-Ahmar, al-Mizan, Lawaqih al-Anwar) report 973 AH. Note the discrepancy.
Discrepancies in death years are common due to different calendar systems or errors in transmission.
4
Understand the source references
The passage cites specific works that mention al-Sha'rani's death. Recognize that later biographers relied on earlier sources, which may have differed.
This shows the importance of verifying multiple sources.
5
Reflect on the incomplete passage
The passage ends mid-sentence ('and 'add baruq al-khawatif:'). This indicates the source is cut off. Consider what information might follow.
Always check manuscript completeness when studying early texts.

Source Text

الإمام الشعراني : هو الشيخ عبد الوهاب بن أحمد الشعراني، صاحب التصانيف الكثيرة. ذكر صاحب الكشف وفاته عند ذكر اليواقيت سنة ست وسبعين وتسعمائة، وعند الكبريت الأحمر، والميزان، ولواقح الأنوار في طبقات السادة الأخيار، ولواقح الأنوار القدسية : سنة ثلاث وسبعين وتسعمائة وعد بروق الخواطف :

The author of al-Kashf mentioned his death when mentioning al-Yawaqit as 976 AH, and according to al-Kibrit al-Ahmar, al-Mizan, Lawaqih al-Anwar fi Tabaqat al-Sada al-Akhyar, and Lawaqih al-Anwar al-Qudsiyya: 973 AH, and 'add baruq al-khawatif:

Imam Zufar: The Master of Qiyas in the Hanafi School
Biographical entry praising Zufar's qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Imam Zufar and explain why his mastery of qiyas is epistemologically significant for Hanafi usul al-fiqh and fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
Imam Zufar was praised by Abu Hanifa as 'the most skilled in qiyas' — a reminder that analogical reasoning is a central tool in Hanafi jurisprudence.

This short biographical entry from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti introduces us to one of the towering figures of the early Hanafi school: Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl. While the passage recounts anecdotes about his life and character, its real legal value lies in the explicit testimony to his mastery of qiyas (analogical reasoning). For a mufti or usuli, understanding Zufar's place helps contextualize the development of Hanafi usul and the weight placed on sound analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Locate the central accolade
Identify Abu Hanifa's statement: 'huwa aqyas ashabi' (he is the most skilled in qiyas among my companions). This is the core of the passage, establishing Zufar's distinguishing skill.
The word 'aqyas' is a superlative; it means 'most skilled in qiyas' and reflects the high value placed on analogical reasoning.
2
Analyse the secondary reports
Review the other narrations: Zufar's precedence in Abu Hanifa's assembly, the wedding sermon, the trustworthiness testimony, and the debate with Abu Yusuf. Each reinforces his authority and intellectual stature.
Note that narrators like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Dawud al-Ta'i are themselves Hanafi scholars, adding credibility.
3
Connect to usul al-fiqh
In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a primary source after Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. A scholar's skill in qiyas directly affects the quality of istinbat (derivation). Zufar's reputation signals the school's rigorous approach.
Zufar often disagreed with Abu Yusuf on qiyas-based rulings, showing that even within the school, qiyas could yield different results.
4
Extract the thamarah (practical outcome)
This biography teaches a modern mufti to appreciate the epistemological hierarchy: textual sources first, then sound qiyas properly applied. Zufar's confidence in debate reflects the culture of intellectual openness early Hanafi circles.
A mufti must carefully evaluate the strength of qiyas before using it to issue a fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأعلام الوارد ذكرهم في الشرح ويقول : هو أقيس أصحابي. وقال الحسن بن زياد "إن المقدم في مجلس الإمام كان زفر " . عن سليمان العطار قال : "تزوج زفر ودعى إلى عرسه الإمام، فالتمس منه أن يخطب فقال في خطبته: "هذا زفر إمام من أئمة المسلمين " . وعلم من إعلامهم في شرفه وحسبه ونسبه . قال أبو نعيم : كان ثقة مأمونا، دخل البصرة في ميراث أخيه، فتشبت به أهل البصرة فمنعوه الخروج منها ، ومات بها سنة ١٥٨هـ، ومولده سنة عشر بعد المائة " . وعن داود الطائي قال : كان أبو يوسف وزفر يتناظران في الفقه وكان زفر جيد اللسان، وكان أبو يوسف يضطرب فى مناظرته. فربما سمعت زفر يقول له : أين تفر، هذه أبواب مفتحة خذ أيها شئت
The notables mentioned in the commentary. And he says: He is the most measured (in qiyas) of my companions. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: 'The one advanced in the assembly of the Imam was Zufar.' From Sulayman al-‘Attar, he said: 'Zufar got married and invited the Imam to his wedding, and asked him to give a sermon. So he said in his sermon: "This Zufar is an imam from the imams of the Muslims."' And it is known from their notables regarding his honor, status, and lineage. Abu Nu‘aym said: 'He was trustworthy and reliable. He entered Basra for the inheritance of his brother, and the people of Basra clung to him and prevented him from leaving there. He died there in the year 158 AH, and his birth was in the year 110 AH.' And from Dawud al-Ta’i, he said: 'Abu Yusuf and Zufar used to debate in fiqh, and Zufar was eloquent in speech, while Abu Yusuf would become agitated in his debate. Sometimes I would hear Zufar say to him: "Where are you fleeing? These are open doors – take whichever you wish."'
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a major Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Hanifa. The text opens by quoting Abu Hanifa’s high praise: 'He is the most skilled in qiyas (analogical reasoning) among my companions.' This establishes Zufar’s reputation as a master of juristic analogy. The narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad confirms that Zufar was given precedence in Abu Hanifa’s study circle. The wedding story underscores his esteemed status. Abu Nu‘aym’s testimony attests to his trustworthiness and his forced stay in Basra, where he died in 158 AH. The anecdote from Dawud al-Ta’i illustrates Zufar’s eloquence and confidence in debate against Abu Yusuf, showing his sharp intellect. This entry is part of the commentary’s identification of notable scholars mentioned in the main text.

Key Terms
زفر (Zufar): Abu al-Hudhayl Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl al-‘Anbari, a leading Hanafi jurist known for expertise in qiyas.
أقيس (aqyas): Superlative of qiyas; 'most skilled in analogical reasoning'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Hanifa say about Imam Zufar's proficiency in qiyas?
A) He is the most reliable in hadith.
B) He is the most skilled in qiyas among my companions.
C) He is the best at writing fatwas.
D) He is the most knowledgeable in inheritance law.

Key Takeaway
Imam Zufar’s biography underscores the centrality of qiyas in Hanafi usul and the high regard for those who master it.

Recognizing Cross-Madhhab Authority: Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki
Biographical entry for Shafi'i scholar Imam Subki

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the scholarly rank of a non-Hanafi mujtahid and identify why his fatwas may be cited in Hanafi fatwa collections.

Core Idea
A Shafi'i mujtahid's fatwas carry weight in Hanafi iftaa when they demonstrate independent ijtihad.

Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki was a towering Shafi'i scholar whose fatwas are frequently referenced in Hanafi works. Understanding his biography helps a mufti gauge the reliability and authority of his legal opinions even outside his own madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar and His School
Read the full name and affiliation: 'al-Subki al-Shafi'i'. Note that he is Shafi'i, not Hanafi. The lesson is about recognizing external scholarly authority.
The name includes 'al-Shafi'i' to denote his madhhab.
2
Examine His Educational Lineage
Look at his teachers: Ibn al-Rif'a (fiqh), al-Sharaf al-Dimyati (hadith), Abu Hayyan (grammar). A strong chain implies sound methodology.
His teachers are respected in their fields.
3
Assess His Scholarly Rank
Note al-Safdi's statement comparing him to al-Ghazali and Sufyan al-Thawri. This indicates he was considered a mujtahid mutlaq by some, which is why his fatwas are cited beyond his madhhab.
Al-Suyuti also counted him among the mujtahids.
4
Verify the Source of His Fatwas
The text mentions his fatwas collected by his son in three volumes, known as 'Fatawa al-Subki'. Recognize that these fatwas are primary sources for his legal reasoning.
Two death dates are given; the reliable one is 756 AH per al-Suyuti.
5
Apply the Fatwa Hierarchy
When citing al-Subki's fatwa, a Hanafi mufti must note the author's authority level (mujtahid) but also apply Hanafi tarjih principles if the fatwa conflicts with the madhhab.
Cross-madhhab citations are used for support, not as primary reliance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-۳۹- الإمام السبكى : هو تقى الدين أبو الحسن علی بن عبد الكافي بن تمام ابن حماد السبكي الشافعي ولد بسبك في صفر سنة ٦٨٣هـ . وتفقه بابن الرفعة وأخذ الحديث عن الشرف الدمياطي، والنحو عن أبي حيان، وانتهت إليه رياسة أهل العلم بمصر. قال الصلاح الصغدى: "الناس يقولون : ما جاء بعد الغزالي مثله، وعندى أنهم يظلمونه وما هو عندي إلا مثل سفيان الثورى" . وله تصانيف جليلة تزيد على الستين ذكرها السيوطي في "حسن المحاضرة". وعده من المجتهدين وأرخ وفاته سنة ٧٥٦هـ، كذا في التعليقات السنية لمولانا عبد الحي وفتاواه المذكورة في المتن مشهورة بفتاوى السبكي، جمعها ولده تاج الدين عبد الوهاب في ثلاث مجلدات، وتوفى سنة إحدى وسبعين وسبعمائة كذا فى الكشف . وش
-39- Imam al-Subki: He is Taqi al-Din Abu al-Hasan ‘Ali ibn ‘Abd al-Kafi ibn Tamam ibn Himad al-Subki al-Shafi‘i. He was born in Subk in Safar in the year 683 AH. He studied fiqh under Ibn al-Rif‘a, took hadith from al-Sharaf al-Dimyati, and grammar from Abu Hayyan. The leadership of the scholars of Egypt culminated in him. al-Salah al-Safdi said: 'The people say that no one like him has come after al-Ghazali, but in my view they are wronging him; he is in my eyes nothing less than Sufyan al-Thawri.' This is in the Ta‘liqat al-Saniyya of Mawlana ‘Abd al-Hayy. His fatwas mentioned in the text are famous as Fatawa al-Subki, collected by his son Taj al-Din ‘Abd al-Wahhab in three volumes. He died in the year 771 AH, as in al-Kashf. And [?].

Commentary
This is a biographical entry on Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki, a prominent Shafi‘i scholar. Although he belongs to the Shafi‘i school, he is included here because his fatwas are referenced in the commentary. The text details his birth, teachers, and his rise to leadership of scholars in Egypt. The praise from al-Salah al-Safdi compares him to al-Ghazali and even Sufyan al-Thawri, indicating his high rank. It mentions his voluminous writings and that al-Suyuti considered him a mujtahid. Key Terms

فتاوى السبكي (Fatawa al-Subki): The collection of fatwas by Imam al-Subki, compiled by his son in three volumes.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sha‘rani’s many works and conflicting death dates show the need for critical evaluation of biographical data.

Imam ‘Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha‘rani is a towering figure in the Hanafi tradition, known both for his legal writings and his spiritual contributions. This brief biographical entry provides essential information about his identity, his major works, and a curious problem: different sources record different years for his death. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: A Mujtahid in the Hanafi Madhhab
Biographical entry on Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani with a debate on his ijtihad rank

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of 'mujtahid fi al-masail' and identify al-Halwani's place in the Hanafi mufti hierarchy, including the debate about following other scholars.

Core Idea
Al-Halwani was a mujtahid within the madhhab, allowed to follow a more knowledgeable scholar.

This lesson introduces Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, a notable Hanafi jurist from the 5th century AH. We learn about his name, death date, and a subtle point about the origin of his nisba. More importantly, the passage clarifies his rank as a mujtahid fi al-masail, a level of ijtihad that permits him to follow other scholars under certain conditions. This distinction is crucial for understanding the hierarchy of authority in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his lifetime
From the passage, note al-Halwani's full name and the various death years reported. This establishes his historical context.
2
Analyze the orthographic debate
Understand the dispute over his nisba: is it derived from 'halwa' (sweet) or from the village Halwan? The passage favors Halwan.
This affects how we write and pronounce his name.
3
Grasp the definition of mujtahid fi al-masail
This term distinguishes him from an absolute mujtahid; he operates within the Hanafi madhhab, able to derive rulings but limited to the school's principles.
He is not an independent mujtahid like Abu Hanifa.
4
Examine the objection and response
The objection that a mujtahid cannot follow others is countered by citing Abu Hanifa's permission and limiting the rule to absolute mujtahids.
This shows the nuance in the hierarchy.
5
Place al-Halwani in the mufti hierarchy
He is not an absolute mujtahid, so he may rely on others for some issues. His writings are authoritative but can be overridden by higher authorities.

-٤١ شمس الأئمة الحلواني : هو عبد العزيز بن أحمد بن نصر بن صالح، قيل : إنه توفى سنة ٤٤٨هـ ، وقيل : سنة ٤٥٢ هـ ، وقيل : سنة ٤٥٦ هـ. و "الحلواني" (بالنون) وقد يقال : بهمز بدل النون، نسبة إلى "الحلواء" ، لا إلى البلد، وسواء كان بالنون أو بالهمز ، فهو مفتوح الحاء، كما صرح به الشيخ عبد الحي في التعليقات" . ونظر فيما قال أخى چلپی فی منہیات ذخيرة العقبي : "من أن الحلواني (بضم الحاء المهملة وسكون اللام آخره نون بعد الألف) اسم بلدة ، لكن رأيت في تمرين الأدب للمولى عبد الأول الجونفورى : أنه نسبة إلى حلوان " وهى قرية لا إلى الحلواء، كما يتوهم. فافهم وتدبر . ثم اعلم أن ابن كمال باشا عده أيضاً من المجتهدين في المسائل. وذكر أخي چلپی في ذخيرة العقبي : "أنه من المجتهدين " ثم اعترض عليه بأنه لو كان من المجتهدين لما جاز له تبعية غيره، ثم أجاب عنه : بأن عدم الجواز ممنوع ، كيف وقد روى عن الإمام الأعظم جواز تقليده لمن هو أعلم منه ، ولئن سلّم فإنما هو فى المجتهد المطلق كالشافعي ومالك . وشمس الأئمة ليس كذلك، كذا ذكره الأستاذ
-41- Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: He is ‘Abd al-‘Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Nasr ibn Salih. It is said he died in 448 AH, and it is said 452 AH, and it is said 456 AH. And 'al-Halwani' (with nun), and it may be said with hamzah instead of nun, a relative attribution to 'al-halwa' (sweet), not to the town. Whether with nun or hamzah, it has a fatha on the ha, as clarified by Shaykh ‘Abd al-Hayy in al-Ta‘liqat. And he considered what my brother Chulpi said in Munyat Dhakhirat al-‘Uqba: 'That al-Halwani (with dammah on the ha, sukun on the lam, and nun at the end after alif) is the name of a town, but I saw in Tamrin al-Adab by al-Mawla ‘Abd al-Awwal al-Jawnfuri that it is a nisba to Halwan, which is a village, not to halwa, as is imagined. So understand and ponder. Then know that Ibn Kamal Pasha also counted him among the mujtahids in masail. And my brother Chulpi mentioned in Dhakhirat al-‘Uqba that he is from the mujtahids, then objected that if he were a mujtahid, it would not be permissible for him to follow someone else. Then he answered that the impermissibility is rejected; how can it be when it is narrated from the Greatest Imam the permissibility of following someone more knowledgeable? And even if conceded, it is only for the absolute mujtahid like al-Shafi‘i and Malik. And Shams al-A'imma is not like that. Thus mentioned by the teacher.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This entry discusses Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, a Hanafi jurist. It first gives possible death years around the mid-5th century AH. Then it delves into the correct pronunciation and etymology of his nisba: whether it is derived from 'halwa' (sweet) or from a place called Halwan. The author clarifies that the nisba is to Halwan, a village, not to sweetness. The passage then addresses a scholarly debate about al-Halwani's level of ijtihad. Ibn Kamal Pasha considered him a mujtahid in masail (i.e., within the madhhab). There is an objection that a mujtahid cannot follow others, but the response permits following a higher authority, and that restriction applies only to absolute mujtahids like al-Shafi‘i and Malik, not to al-Halwani. This shows the nuanced hierarchy of ijtihad in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مجتهد في المسائل (mujtahid fi al-masail): A jurist capable of deriving rulings within the Hanafi madhhab, not an absolute mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because he is allowed to change his rulings

Key Takeaway
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani represents the level of mujtahid fi al-masail, a rank that permits limited taqlid and deepens our understanding of Hanafi ijtihad hierarchy.

Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: Dictating al-Mabsut from Memory
Biographical entry for Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the circumstances under which al-Sarakhsi composed al-Mabsut and identify the implications for the authority of his work in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Al-Sarakhsi dictated al-Mabsut from prison — memory alone preserved Hanafi fiqh.

This biographical entry introduces Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, one of the greatest Hanafi jurists. His monumental work al-Mabsut was dictated entirely from memory while he was imprisoned for advising a ruler. His achievement underscores the importance of memorization in Hanafi scholarship and the resilience required for preserving legal knowledge under duress. Understanding his story enriches our appreciation of the textual hierarchy in Hanafi fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his work
Name the scholar (al-Sarakhsi) and his major fiqh work (al-Mabsut). Note his full name and death date.
2
Understand the composition circumstances
Recognize that al-Mabsut was dictated from memory while he was imprisoned in Uzjand. He had no access to books.
3
Analyze the significance for Hanafi fiqh
Consider how the dictation from memory adds to the authority of the work — it demonstrates his mastery. Also note his other works in usul and siyar.
4
Relate to mufti practice
Reflect on how a mufti today cites al-Mabsut. The work's authority is enhanced by its rigorous oral transmission from a master.
This is not a legal ruling but a biographical lesson that informs the adab of the mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٢ شمس الأئمة السرخسي : هو محمد بن أحمد أبي سهل السرخسي، المتوفى سنة ٤٨٣ هـ، أملى المبسوط من خاطره من غير مطالعة كتاب (وهو في السجن بـ أوز جند" بسبب كلمة نصح بها "الخاقان ) وذكر فيه حسب حاله في آخر كل كتب من الكتاب، وقال في آخر شرح العبادات : "هذا آخر شرح العبادات بأوضح المعاني وأوجز العبارات، إملاء المحبوس عن الجمع والجماعات . وقال في آخر شرح الإقرار : شرح الإقرار المشتمل من المعاني على ما هو من الأسرار، إملاء المحبوس في مجلس الأشرار" . وله كتاب في أصول الفقه، وشرح السير الكبير . والسرخسي : نسبة إلى سرخس " (بفتح السين وفتح الراء وسكون الخاء بلدة من بلاد الخراسان، وهو اسم رجل سكن هذا الموضع ، وعمره وبناه ذو القرنين، كذا في الفوائد. قلت : وفـيـه لـغـة أخرى أيضا ذكرها النووي في شرحه وهي: "سرخس (بفتح السين وسكون الراء المهملة وفتح الخاء المعجمة).
42- Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: He is Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Sahl al-Sarakhsi, who died in 483 AH. He dictated al-Mabsut from his mind without consulting a book (while he was in prison in Uzjand due to a word of advice he gave to the Khagan). And he mentioned his state at the end of each book of the work. He said at the end of Sharh al-‘Ibadat: 'This is the end of the commentary on acts of worship with the clearest meanings and most concise expressions, dictated by the one imprisoned from congregation and communities.' And he said at the end of Sharh al-Iqrar: 'Commentary on declaration, containing meanings that are secrets, dictated by the imprisoned in the assembly of the wicked.' And he has a book on usul al-fiqh and a commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir. And al-Sarakhsi is a nisba to Sarakhs (with fatha on the sin and ra, and sukun on the kha, a town in Khorasan, and it is the name of a man who settled there, and it was built and populated by Dhul-Qarnayn, as in al-Fawa'id. I say: And there is another pronunciation mentioned by al-Nawawi in his commentary: 'Sarakhs (with fatha on the sin, sukun on the ra, and fatha on the kha).'
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This entry is about Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, one of the greatest Hanafi jurists. His monumental work al-Mabsut was dictated entirely from memory while he was imprisoned for advising a ruler. The text quotes his poignant remarks at the end of sections, highlighting his hardship. He also authored works on usul al-fiqh and a commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir. The passage explains the nisba 'al-Sarakhsi' to the town Sarakhs in Khorasan, noting alternative pronunciations. This entry emphasizes his scholarly achievement under duress and his lasting contribution to Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The extensive Hanafi fiqh work dictated by al-Sarakhsi from memory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) While imprisoned
C) While teaching in a mosque
D) While studying in Basra

Key Takeaway
Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut, dictated from memory in prison, is a testament to the Hanafi tradition of oral transmission and the resilience of its scholars.

Parsing the Title 'Shams al-A'imma' in Hanafi Works
Biographical entries with a key parsing rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether the title 'Shams al-A'imma' is used absolutely (referring to al-Sarakhsi) or qualified (with a name/nisbah) in Hanafi texts and apply this convention to determine the intended scholar.

Core Idea
In Hanafi books, 'Shams al-A'imma' alone means al-Sarakhsi; any other scholar requires a qualifier.

In Hanafi fatwa and fiqh texts, titles like 'Shams al-A'imma' appear frequently. Knowing which scholar is intended by the bare title is essential for understanding the authority behind a ruling. This lesson examines the canonical rule stated in the source: when the title is unqualified, it refers exclusively to al-Sarakhsi. We will parse the relevant entry on al-Halwani and the explicit benefit (fa'idah) to master this parsing skill.

Guided Path
1
Locate the title and its modifiers
Scan the Arabic passage for every occurrence of 'Shams al-A'imma'. Note whether the title appears alone or is followed by a name (e.g., al-Halwani) or nisbah (e.g., al-Kurdari). This immediate visual clue determines if it is absolute or qualified.
The benefit on page 234 states the rule explicitly.
2
Recall the Hanafi convention
Internalize the rule: when 'Shams al-A'imma' is used without any qualifier in the books of the Hanafi school, it refers to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. No other scholar is meant by the bare title.
This is a fixed convention, not a matter of guesswork.
3
Apply to the al-Halwani entry
In the al-Halwani entry, the title is qualified as 'Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani'. The passage also debates the etymology of 'al-Halwani' (from 'halwa' or a village). Note that the qualifier is essential—otherwise the reader would mistakenly think of al-Sarakhsi.
The inclusion of the nisbah 'al-Halwani' makes him a different person.
4
Distinguish from other scholars
The same rule applies to al-Kurdari and al-Hariri: they are always mentioned with qualifiers. Understand that the absolute usage is reserved for al-Sarakhsi due to his towering authority and the unique circumstances of his work.
This hierarchy reflects the mufta bihi (operative) status of al-Sarakhsi’s rulings.
5
Apply to a new text
When reading any Hanafi work, if you encounter the phrase 'قال شمس الأئمة' without further qualification, you now know it means 'al-Sarakhsi said'. This instant identification is crucial for weighing evidence in fatwa derivation.
Failure to apply this rule leads to confusing scholars and misattributing authority.

٤٤ شمس الدين الحريري: هو شمس الدین محمد بن عثمان المعروف - بابن الحريري، المتوفى سنة ثمان وعشرين وسبعمائة . كذا في الكشف، وفي الفوائد محمد بن عثمان بن أبي الحسن بن عبد الوهاب شمس الدين، المعروف بابن الحريري . أخذ عن ابن المعلم إسماعيل القرشي عن الجمال محمود الحصيري. وكان عالما، ،فاضلا فقيهاً، عارفا بالمذهب، انتهت إليه الرئاسة في زمانه . تولى قضاء دمشق. ومات سنة ثمان وعشرين وسبعمائة، ومولده بدمشق سنة ثلاث وخمسين وستمائة . وفى "حسن المحاضرة للسيوطى : شمس الدین محمد بن عثمان بن أبي الحسن الدمشقى الحريري، قاضي الديار المصرية . وكان رأسًا في المذهب عادلا مهيبا . حدث عن ابن الصيرفي وابن أبي السير، والقطب بن أبي عصرون. ولد في صفر سنة ثلاث
