الأعلام الوارد ذكرهم في الشرح العارف بالله تعالى سليمان الخضيري . قال الشيخ عبد الوهاب صحبته عشر سنين فما رأيت عليه شيئًا يشينه في دينه، وحججت معه في سنة ثلاث وخمسين وتسعمائة فرأيته على خلق عظيم مع جيرانه و غلمانه ذهابًا وإيابًا ، مع أن السفر يسفر عن أخلاق الرجال . ولقد شاورنى فى ترك التدريس والإقبال على طريق الفقراء الصوفية فقلت له : لا تدخل في الطريق إلا بعد تضلعك من علوم الشريعة، فأجابني إلى ذلك. أسأل الله تعالى أن يزيده علما وعملا صالحا، ويحشرنا في زمرته مع العلماء العاملين والأئمة المجتهدين تحت لواء سيد المرسلين. ولمولانا المترجم " الأشباه والنظائر " و "البحر الرائق" و "مختصر التحرير" و "شرح المنار" و "الفوائد الزينية و الرسائل الزينية " التي رتبها ابن بنته محمد . وأما تعاليقه على هوامش الكتب وحواشيها، وكتابته على أسئلة المستفتين، والأوراق التي سودها بالمباحث الرائقة فشيء لا يمكن حصره، ولولا معاجلة الأجل قبل بلوغ الأمل لكان في الفقه وأصوله وفي سائر الفنون أعجوبة الدهر . توفي سنة سبعين وتسعمائة وقال تلميذه العلمي : "إن وفاته كانت في سنة تسع - بتقديم التاء- وستين وتسعمائة ، وإن ولادته كانت سنة ست وعشرين وتسعمائة، ودفن بالقرب من السيدة كينة رحم الله تعالى روحه ونور ضريحه آمين . كذا في شرح الأشباه والنظائر لشيخنا العلامة المحقق هبة الله أفندى البعلى التاجي رحمه الله تعالى. قال الشيخ العلامة قطب الدين الحنفى : أنشدني من لفظه الشيخ زين بن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى بهذه الأبيات بديهة وقد أجاد فقال :
ذو الفضل زين الدين حاز من التقى والعلم ما عجز الورى عن حصره لا سيما الفقه الشريف فإنه یملیکه بکماله من صدره وإذا نظرت إلى الشروح بأسرها فترى الجميع كنقطة في بحره ونقل من خط الشيخ الفهامة سرى الدين الصائغ الحنفي ما صورته : أنشدني منصور البلسى الحنفى لنفسه: على الكنز في الفقه الشروح كثيرة بحار تفيد الطالبين لآليا ولكن بهذا البحر صارت سواقيا ومن ورد البحر استقل السواقيا
The notable personalities mentioned in the commentary: the gnostic of Allah Almighty, Sulayman al-Khudayri. Sheikh Abdul Wahhab said: I kept his company for ten years and never saw anything that would disgrace him in his religion, and I performed Hajj with him in the year 953 AH and saw him with great character towards his neighbors and servants, going and coming, while travel reveals the morals of men. He consulted me about leaving teaching and turning to the path of the Sufi poor, and I said to him: Do not enter the path until you are well-versed in the sciences of Sharia, and he agreed to that. I ask Allah Almighty to increase him in knowledge and righteous deeds, and to gather us in his group with the acting scholars and the mujtahid imams under the banner of the Master of the Messengers. And for our author (the subject of this translation) are [the works] "Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir", "Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq", "Mukhtasar al-Tahrir", "Sharh al-Manar", "Al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyyah" and "Al-Rasa'il al-Zayniyyah" which were arranged by his daughter's son Muhammad. As for his glosses on the margins of books and their footnotes, and his writing in response to questions of mustaftis, and the papers he blackened with excellent discussions, it is something that cannot be counted. And were it not for the hastening of death before the attainment of hope, he would have been, in Fiqh and its principles and in all arts, the wonder of the age. He died in the year 970 AH, and his scholarly student said: "His death was in the year 969 AH (with the ta' advanced), and his birth was in the year 926 AH, and he was buried near al-Sayyida Kina. May Allah have mercy on his soul and illuminate his grave, Amen." Thus in Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by our teacher, the all-knowing investigator, Hibbatullah Afandi al-Ba'li al-Taji, may Allah have mercy on him. The all-knowing scholar Qutb al-Din al-Hanafi said: The Sheikh Zayn ibn Nujaym, may Allah have mercy on him, recited these verses extemporaneously to me, and he did well, saying: "The man of virtue, Zayn al-Din, attained from piety and knowledge what creation is incapable of counting, especially the noble Fiqh, for he completely possesses it from his chest. And when you look at the commentaries altogether, you see all of them like a point in his sea." And it was transmitted from the handwriting of the learned Sheikh, Sirr al-Din al-Sa'igh al-Hanafi, the following: Mansur al-Balsi al-Hanafi recited to me of his own composition: "On 'Al-Kanz' in Fiqh, the commentaries are many, seas that benefit the seekers with pearls, but by this sea they became streams, and whoever enters the sea considers the streams insignificant."
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry from a commentary on Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. It begins by mentioning the gnostic Sulayman al-Khudayri, a teacher of Zayn ibn Nujaym, and quotes a student's testimony to his excellent character. The core biography then focuses on Zayn ibn Nujaym (the 'mutarjim' or subject of translation), listing his major Hanafi works: Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair (a landmark work of legal maxims), Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq), Mukhtasar al-Tahrir, Sharh al-Manar, and Al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyyah with its epistles. It notes his prolific marginalia and fatwas, lamenting his early death. There is a discrepancy in his death year: 970 AH versus 969 AH according to a student. His birth is given as 926 AH. The passage ends with two poetic eulogies praising Zayn's mastery of Fiqh. This biography confirms the scholarly authority of Zayn ibn Nujaym within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المترجم (al-mutarjam): The person whose biography is being written, here Zayn ibn Nujaym.
الأشباه والنظائر (al-ashbah wa al-naza'ir): A work on Hanafi legal maxims and similar cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biography of Mulla Khusraw and His Works
Biographical entry on Mulla Khusraw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Mulla Khusraw and explain the relationship between his works Al-Durar and Gharar al-Ahkam in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Mulla Khusraw's nickname came from his son-in-law, and his commentary Al-Durar on his own matn remains a standard Hanafi reference.

This biographical entry introduces Mulla Khusraw, a towering Hanafi jurist of the 9th century AH. Understanding his life, the origin of his name, and his major works helps you recognize the chain of authority in Hanafi texts. His Durar al-Hukkam (commentary) and Gharar al-Ahkam (matn) are widely used in Hanafi fatwa and judicial practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and lineage
Read the first sentence to find his full name (Muhammad ibn Framuz) and his famous epithet (Mulla Khusraw). Note that he is described as an 'overflowing ocean' in knowledge.
He is the author of Al-Durar wa al-Gharar.
2
Analyze the name transformation
Trace how he came to be called 'Mulla Khusraw': originally known as 'brother of Khusraw's wife' after his father-in-law (the Amir), then the name Khusraw prevailed.
This shows the importance of social connections in naming.
3
Note his death and burial
Find the year (885 AH) and places (Constantinople and Bursa). This is crucial for historical context.
Death dates help establish textual chronology.
4
Understand the works
Identify Al-Durar as Durar al-Hukkam (commentary) and Gharar al-Ahkam (matn). Note that the commentary explains his own matn, a common practice in Hanafi scholarship.
The phrase 'falyuhfaz' indicates it is a foundational text to memorize.
5
Connect to fatwa practice
Reflect on why this work is important: it is a standard reference for Hanafi judges (al-hukkam) and muftis, as the title 'Durar al-Hukkam' suggests.
Knowing the author and his work helps assess the authority of a fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٨ - صاحب الدرر والغرر : هو محمد بن فراموز، الشهير بـ المولى خسرو" ، كان بحراً ذاخراً، عالما بالمعقول والمنقول، وحبراً فاخراً جامعا للفروع والأصول، وكان أبوه رومى الأصل ثم أسلم. وكانت له بنت زوجها من أمير يسمى به خسرو"، وابنه محمد هذا كان في حجر خسرو"، وبعد وفاة أبيه اشتهر بـ أخي زوجة خسرو " ، ثم غلب عليه اسم خسرو . مات سنة خمس وثمانين وثمان مائة بقسطنطينية ثم نقل إلى مدينة "بروسا" . و "الدرر " : هو درر الحكام المعروف بـ درر مولا خسرو وشرح لمتنه " غرر الأحكام" . فليحفظ .
48 - The author of Al-Durar wa al-Gharar: He is Muhammad ibn Framuz, famously known as Mulla Khusraw. He was an overflowing ocean, knowledgeable in rational and transmitted sciences, and an excellent scholar encompassing branches and principles. His father was of Roman origin then embraced Islam. He had a daughter whom he married to an Amir named Khusraw, and this son Muhammad was under the guardianship of Khusraw. After the death of his father, he became known as 'the brother of Khusraw's wife', then the name Khusraw prevailed over him. He died in the year 885 AH in Constantinople, then was transferred to the city of Bursa. And 'Al-Durar' is Durar al-Hukkam, known as Durar Mulla Khusraw, and it is a commentary on his matn 'Gharar al-Ahkam'. May it be memorized.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for the Hanafi jurist Mulla Khusraw (Muhammad ibn Framuz). It gives his lineage, his general scholarly excellence ('overflowing ocean'), and a curious note about his name: originally 'brother of Khusraw's wife' from his son-in-law's name, then 'Mulla Khusraw' stuck. He died in 885 AH in Constantinople and was moved to Bursa. His famous work Al-Durar (Durar al-Hukkam) is a commentary on his own matn Gharar al-Ahkam, a standard Hanafi legal text. The entry ends with the note 'falyuhfaz' (may it be memorized), indicating the importance of remembering this scholar and his work.

Key Terms
الدرر والغرر (al-durar wa al-gharar): The title of Mulla Khusraw's commentary (Al-Durar) and its matn (Gharar al-Ahkam).
المولى خسرو (al-mulla khusraw): The epithet of Muhammad ibn Framuz, meaning 'Master Khusraw'.
درر الحكام (durar al-hukkam): The title of the commentary, meaning 'Pearls of the Judges'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Constantinople
C) Baghdad
D) Cairo

Key Takeaway
Mulla Khusraw's Al-Durar wa al-Gharar is a foundational Hanafi reference, and his nickname is derived from his son-in-law's name.

The Legacy of al-Hadadi: Two Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical entry of a Hanafi jurist and author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works of al-Hadadi al-Abbadi and state their significance in Hanafi fiqh literature.

Core Idea
Al-Hadadi's two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri remain essential Hanafi references for different levels.

This biographical entry introduces Imam Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Hadadi al-Abbadi, a prolific Hanafi scholar who devoted his life to teaching and writing. Understanding his role and the scope of his works helps us appreciate the depth and organization of the Hanafi textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Read the opening phrase: 'Imam Abu Bakr ibn Ali, known as al-Hadadi al-Abbadi'. Note his full name and epithet.
Al-Hadadi likely refers to his hometown or trade; al-Abbadi indicates his lineage.
2
List his major works
From the text, extract the titles: Tafsir 'Kashf al-Tanzil', 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' (4 vols), 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' (8 vols).
Both commentaries are on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi matn.
3
Compare the two commentaries
Note that al-Siraj is double the size of al-Jawhara. This indicates a more detailed exposition, while al-Jawhara likely offers a concise explanation.
Muftis may use al-Jawhara for quick reference and al-Siraj for in-depth study.
4
Recognize his teaching and piety
The text mentions he taught fifteen lessons daily and was known for asceticism and miracles (karamat). This establishes his authority and dedication.
Such descriptions are common in Hanafi biographical works to highlight scholarly credibility.
5
Assess the impact of his works
The phrase 'His works spread far and wide' indicates these commentaries became standard references in the Hanafi school.
Both texts are still in print and used in madrasas today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٩ - صاحب السراج الوهاج والجوهرة : هو الإمام أبو بكر بن على، المعروف بالحدادي العبادي، المتوفى في حدود ثمان مائة. قال مولانا عبد الحى في النافع الكبير " : "قال على القاري في "طبقات الحنفية " : كان عالما، عاملا، ناسكا، فاضلا زاهداً ، كان يقرئ فى كل يوم خمسة عشر درسًا . وله مصنفات كثيرة منها : التفسير المسمّى بـ "كشف التنزيل"، و "الجوهرة النيرة " شرح مختصر القدوري في أربع مجلدات ، و "السراج الوهاج شرح مختصر القدوري في ثماني مجلدات، وغير ذلك، وسارت بمؤلفاته الركبان. مات سنة ثمان مائة . وله كرامات كثيرة .
49 - The author of Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Al-Jawhara: He is Imam Abu Bakr ibn Ali, known as al-Hadadi al-Abbadi, who died around eight hundred [AH]. Our master Abd al-Hayy said in 'Al-Nafi' al-Kabir': 'Ali al-Qari said in 'Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya': He was a scholar, a practitioner, a devout worshiper, a virtuous ascetic. He would teach fifteen lessons every day. He has many works, including the Tafsir named 'Kashf al-Tanzil', and 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri in four volumes, and 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri in eight volumes, and others. His works spread far and wide. He died in the year 800 AH. He had many miracles.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This entry introduces Imam Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Hadadi al-Abbadi, a Hanafi scholar who died around 800 AH. He is known for his extensive teaching (15 lessons daily) and his two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: al-Jawhara al-Nayyira (4 volumes) and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (8 volumes). He also wrote a tafsir. The entry highlights his piety and asceticism, and even mentions miracles (karamat). His works are standard references in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-jawhara al-nayyira): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Hadadi, in 4 volumes.
السراج الوهاج (al-siraj al-wahhaj): A larger commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by the same author, in 8 volumes.
مختصر القدوري (mukhtasar al-quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh matn by Imam al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Al-Bazzazi and His Fatwa Collection
Biographical entry of the compiler of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the compiler of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, state its completion date, and explain its status as a relied-upon source in the Hanafi fatwa tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya is a relied-upon Hanafi fatwa collection compiled by al-Bazzazi in 812 AH.

This lesson introduces you to Muhammad al-Bazzazi, the compiler of one of the most important Hanafi fatwa collections. Understanding who he was and the nature of his work will help you appreciate how later muftis rely on compiled fatwa literature. The passage provides key biographical details and the authoritative status of the collection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Compiler
Read the full name and lineage of al-Bazzazi as given in the text. Note that he is known as al-Bazzazi and also as Ibn al-Bazzaz. This helps locate him in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.
The name includes his nisbahs: al-Kardari, al-Bariqini, al-Khwarizmi.
2
Trace His Scholarly Journey
Follow the narrative of his education under his father, his travel to the town of Qadim, his sixty-year stay there, and his debates with imams. This contextualizes the depth of his learning.
The river mentioned is likely the Ail River, but the exact location is not critical.
3
Recognize the Fatwa Collection
Note the title of his work: al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, also called al-Jami' al-Wajiz. Understand that it is a compilation of fatwas from various books, with the author choosing the stronger opinions.
The collection is not a fiqh matn but a fatwa reference.
4
Confirm the Date and Authority
Find the completion year: 812 AH. Also note the statement that 'the imams mentioned that it is relied upon' (عليه التعويل). This tells you its authoritative rank in the school.
The date is given in the middle of the text: عام ثنتى عشرة وثمان مائة.
5
Note the Unfinished Question
The passage ends with a question posed to Abu al-Su'ud al-Mufti about why he did not collect ambiguous issues. This indicates that the collection was used and discussed by later muftis.
The answer is not included in this excerpt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥٠ - صاحب الفتاوى البزازية : هو محمد بن محمد بن شهاب بن يوسف الكردري البريقيني الخوارزمی الحنفى الشهير بالبزازي، كذا في الفوائد. وفي الكشف : "أنه المعروف بابن البزاز". وكان رحمه الله من أفراد الدهر في الفروع والأصول، حاز قصبات السبق فى العلوم، أخذ عن أبيه ومهر واشتهر في بلاده، وكان في بلدة سراى قريب نهر آئل، ثم رحل إلى بلدة "قديم" بلدة خارج ترخان في ساحل النهر المذكور وأقام بها ستين، وناظر فيها الأئمة الأعلام، وحارس الفقهاء ثم رجع إلى بلاده، وصنف "الفتاوى البزازية" ، وهو كتاب جامع لخص فيه زبدة مسائل الفتاوى والواقعات من الكتب المختلفة، ورجح ما ساعده الدليل، وذكر الأئمة أن عليه التعويل، وسماه "الجامع الوجيز " ، فرغ من جمعه وتأليفه كما ذكره في أواسط كتابه عام ثنتى عشرة وثمان مائة. قيل لأبي السعود المفتى: "لم لم تجمع المسائل المبهمة ولم تؤلف فيها
50 - The author of Al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya: He is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Shihab ibn Yusuf al-Kardari al-Bariqini al-Khwarizmi al-Hanafi, famously known as al-Bazzazi. So in al-Fawa'id. And in al-Kashf: 'He is known as Ibn al-Bazzaz.' He, may Allah have mercy on him, was unique in his time in branches and principles; he achieved the highest ranks in sciences. He took from his father, excelled, and became famous in his lands. He was in the town of Saray near the River Ail, then he traveled to the town of 'Qadim', a town outside Tarkhan on the bank of the mentioned river, and stayed there for sixty [years?]. He debated the distinguished imams and guarded the jurists, then returned to his lands. He compiled 'Al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya', which is a comprehensive book in which he summarized the cream of fatwa issues and occurrences from various books, and gave preponderance to what evidence supported. The imams mentioned that it is relied upon. He named it 'Al-Jami' al-Wajiz'. He completed its collection and composition, as he mentioned in the middle of his book, in the year 812 AH. It was said to Abu al-Su'ud al-Mufti: 'Why did you not collect the ambiguous issues and write about them...'
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This entry is for Muhammad al-Bazzazi, compiler of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, a major Hanafi fatwa collection. He was from Khwarazm, famous as Ibn al-Bazzaz. The text details his travels, debates, and sixty-year stay in Qadim. His work summarizes fatwas from many sources and is considered authoritative. The completion date is 812 AH. The entry ends abruptly with a question to Abu al-Su'ud al-Mufti about not collecting ambiguous issues, but the response is not included in the passage.

Key Terms
الفتاوى البزازية (al-fatawa al-bazzaziyya): A comprehensive collection of Hanafi fatwas compiled by al-Bazzazi.
الجامع الوجيز (al-jami' al-wajiz): Alternate title of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya.
البزازي (al-bazzazi): Nickname of the author, meaning 'the cloth seller' or 'the weaver'.

Evaluating the Reliability of al-Qunyah in Hanafi Iftaa
Biographical assessment of a Hanafi text's reliability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the authority of al-Qunyah in Hanafi fatwa using the criteria of riwayah and author's creed.

Core Idea
Not every Hanafi book is reliable; a mufti must weigh transmission strength and author's 'aqidah.

When a mufti encounters a ruling in al-Qunyah, how should he treat it? This lesson introduces the biography of al-Zahidi and the scholarly assessment of his work. You will learn why al-Qunyah is not a primary source in the Hanafi school and how to handle its rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his work
Note the full name, title, and death date of al-Zahidi. Recognize that his work is titled 'al-Qunyah' and is extracted from 'Munyat al-Fuqaha'.
2
Understand the assessment of al-Mulla Barkali
Barkali says al-Qunyah is 'above the non-considered books' but 'famous for weak transmission' and its author is Mu'tazili. Identify the two key issues: riwayah (transmission) and 'aqidah (creed).
Weak transmission means the chain of narrators is not fully reliable.
3
Apply the principle: works of al-Zahidi are not reliable unless corroborated
Barkali states that al-Zahidi's works are 'not considered reliable' unless they agree with other reliable sources, because they mix sound and unsound material.
4
Conclude the status of al-Qunyah in the Hanafi hierarchy
Al-Qunyah is not part of Zahir al-Riwayah. It is a secondary source that may be used cautiously when supported by stronger texts.
Refer to 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir' for further detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب القنية : هو الشيخ الإمام أبو الرجاء، نجم الدين مختار ابن محمود الزاهدى الحنفى المتوفى سنة ٦٥٨هـ . قال المولى بركلي : " والقنية وإن كانت فوق الكتب الغير المعتبرة ( وقد نقل عنها بعض العلماء في كتبهم لكنها مشهورة عند العلماء بضعف الرواية، وإن صاحبها معتزلى ذكر في أولها : أنه استصفاها من "منية الفقهاء لأستاذه بديع بن أبي منصور العراقي، وسماها "قنية المنية لتيمم الغنية " . وتصانيفه غير معتبرة ما لم يوجد مطابقتها لغيرها ؛ لكونها جامعة للرطب واليابس. وتفصيل ذلك في "النافع الكبير " .
The author of al-Qunyah: he is the Shaykh Imam Abu al-Raja, Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi al-Hanafi, who died in the year 658 AH. Al-Mulla Barkali said: 'Al-Qunyah, although it is above the non-considered books, and some scholars have transmitted from it in their books, yet it is famous among scholars for weak transmission, and its author is a Mu'tazili. He mentioned in its beginning that he extracted it from "Munyat al-Fuqaha" of his teacher Badi' ibn Abi Mansur al-Iraqi, and he named it "Qunyat al-Munya li-Tayammum al-Ghunya". His works are not considered reliable unless found to be in agreement with others, because they compile both sound and unsound material. The detail of that is in "al-Nafi' al-Kabir".'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This is a biographical entry on the author of the well-known Hanafi fiqh work 'al-Qunyah'. The entry identifies him as Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi al-Hanafi, who died in 658 AH. The text then quotes al-Mulla Barkali's assessment: though the book is above completely unreliable works, it is known among scholars for weak transmission (sahif al-riwaya). Moreover, its author is a Mu'tazili. The author himself states that he extracted his work from his teacher's 'Munyat al-Fuqaha'. Barkali warns that al-Zahidi's works are not considered authoritative unless they agree with other reliable sources, because they mix sound and unsound material. The fuller discussion is in 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir'. This is important for a Hanafi mufti to know when using al-Qunyah as a reference: it is not from the core reliable texts of the madhhab.

Key Terms
القنية (al-Qunyah): A Hanafi fiqh work compiled by al-Zahidi, extracted from Munyat al-Fuqaha, but considered weak in transmission.
ضعف الرواية (du'f al-riwayah): Weakness in the chain of transmission, making the text less authoritative.
معتزلي (Mu'tazili): A follower of Mu'tazilite theology, which differs from Sunni orthodoxy on certain creedal points.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is al-Qunyah not considered a primary reliable source in the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is too old and outdated.
B) Because its author was a Mu'tazili and its transmission is weak.
C) Because it was written in a different madhhab.
D) Because it contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Al-Qunyah is a secondary Hanafi text; a mufti should only use it when its rulings are corroborated by stronger sources.

Biography of al-Nasafi: Author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq
Biographical entry on al-Nasafi, author of al-Kanz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Nasafi's full name, the dispute over his death date, and his rank in the Hanafi school as reported in this biographical entry.

Core Idea
Al-Nasafi's authority in the Hanafi school is debated: some place him as a mujtahid within the madhhab, others as a transmitter.

In Hanafi scholarship, the author of a matn carries weight. This lesson introduces the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Nasafi. We will examine his name, the dispute about his death date, and differing views on his scholarly rank. Understanding his status helps a mufti correctly assess the authority of his text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and nisba
Extract the author's full name and the correct pronunciation of 'Nasaf' from the text. Note the variant readings.
The nisba is crucial for identifying the scholar correctly.
2
Compare the reported death dates
List the three death dates mentioned (701, after 710, 710) and note the sources for each. Recognize the lack of consensus.
Disputes over death dates are common in early biographical sources.
3
Analyze the difference in his rank classification
Contrast the two classifications: (1) among as-hab al-tamyiz according to Ibn Kamal Pasha; (2) a mujtahid in the madhhab, with the claim that no such mujtahid appeared after him.
As-hab al-tamyiz can distinguish strong from weak transmissions but do not perform independent ijtihad.
4
Determine the significance for a mufti
Reflect on why knowing al-Nasafi's rank matters: if he is a mujtahid in the madhhab, his text carries more weight; if not, it is still a reliable matn but of lower authority.
The mufti must know the hierarchical status of sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب الكنز : هو عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود أبو البركات حافظ الدين النسفي، نسبة إلى "نسف" (بفتحتين) من بلاد "السعد" فيما وراء النهر، وقيل: بكسر السين، وفى النسبة تفتح . أرخ القارى وفاته سنة ٧٠١هـ، وقال قاسم بن قطلوبغا : إن موت النسفى بعد عشر وسبعمائة وذكر فى الكشف : "وفاته سنة عشر وسبعمائة " . وعده ابن كمال باشا من أصحاب التمييز، وعده غيره من المجتهدين في المذهب، وقال: إنه اختتم به ولم يوجد بعده مجتهد في المذهب " .
The author of al-Kanz: he is Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud Abu al-Barakat Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi, relative to 'Nasaf' (with two fatha) from the land of 'Sa'd' in Transoxiana, and it is said: with kasr of the seen, and in the relative it is opened. Al-Qari dated his death as 701 AH, and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said that al-Nasafi's death was after 710, and it is mentioned in al-Kashf: 'His death was in the year 710.' Ibn Kamal Pasha counted him among the people of tamyiz, and others counted him among the mujtahids in the madhhab, and said: 'The madhhab ended with him and no mujtahid in the madhhab was found after him.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This entry covers al-Nasafi, the author of the famous Hanafi matn 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq'. The entry mentions the correct nisba (Nasaf) with pronunciation details. His death date is disputed: al-Qari says 701 AH, while Qasim ibn Qutlubugha says after 710, and al-Kashf records 710. His rank is also debated: Ibn Kamal Pasha considers him among the 'as-hab al-tamyiz' (those capable of distinguishing between strong and weak transmissions within the madhhab), while others consider him a mujtahid within the madhhab, even saying no such mujtahid appeared after him. This is important for a mufti to know the authority of al-Nasafi's works, especially Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which is a key text in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الكنز (al-Kanz): Short for Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a concise Hanafi fiqh text by al-Nasafi, widely used.
أصحاب التمييز (as-hab al-tamyiz): Those who can distinguish between strong and weak narrations within the madhhab, but are not capable of independent ijtihad.
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A jurist who can derive rulings within the confines of the Hanafi school, using its principles and sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the disagreement about al-Nasafi?
A) His death date and his rank in ijtihad.
B) The name of his book.
C) Whether he was Hanafi or Shafi'i.
D) The meaning of his name.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi's authority is high; his text Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a key source, but a mufti must know the dispute about his rank and date to correctly weigh his contributions.

The Mufti's Toolkit: Majma' al-Bahrayn and Its Author
Biographical entry of Ibn al-Sa'ati and description of his work Majma' al-Bahrayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the biographical context of Ibn al-Sa'ati and explain how the structure of Majma' al-Bahrayn serves a mufti's need to address difficult fiqh issues.

Core Idea
A mufti values a book that flags the hard questions—Majma' al-Bahrayn does exactly that.

This lesson introduces you to Ibn al-Sa'ati and his unique Hanafi fiqh work, Majma' al-Bahrayn. Understanding the background and structure of this book equips you with another tool for fatwa research. We'll explore why a mufti would turn to this text and how its arrangement anticipates the very challenges you'll face in real-world ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and His Lineage
Read the biography: Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Tha'lab, known as Ibn al-Sa'ati. Note his origins (Baalbek, Baghdad), his death year (694 AH), and his father's fame as a clock-maker and astronomer. This scholarly environment shaped his work.
The father's skill in precise mechanical work parallels the author's systematic arrangement of fiqh.
2
Recognize the Book's Full Title and Structure
Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn. It collects al-Quduri's versified fiqh text and adds supplementary material. The key feature: at the end of each book, he lists 'difficult issues' (mushkilat) related to that section.
This is a practical help for a mufti who often encounters tricky edge cases.
3
Appreciate the Pedagogical Value for a Mufti
The work is not just a summary; it highlights problematic points. A mufti can quickly scan these lists to see if a particular issue has been addressed. This saves time and ensures thoroughness.
The daughter Fatima's annotations show the book was used for teaching and commentary.
4
Connect to the Ifta Discipline
In fatwa, you must consider all possible angles. Majma' al-Bahrayn's built-in problem-spotting helps you foresee difficulties in a case. It exemplifies a 'mufti-friendly' arrangement.
Modern muftis still consult this work for its clarity and focus on problematic cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب المجمع : هو أحمد بن على بن ثعلب مظفر الدين، المعروف بـ ابن الساعاتي ، البعلبكي أصلا، والبغدادى منشأ، مات سنة ٦٩٤هـ . وكانت له بنت مسماة بـ"فاطمة" . تفقهت على أبيها ، وأخذت عنه مجمع البحرين، وكانت تكتب تعليقا حسنًا. وأبوه على بن ثعلب هو الذي عمل الساعات على باب المستنصر" ببغداد، وكان مشتهراً بالهيئة والنجوم، وعمل الساعات والمجمع : كتاب جمع فيه مسائل القدوري المنظومة مع زيادات ورتب فأحسن ترتيبه، وأبدع في اختصاره ويذكر في آخر كل كتاب منه ما شد عنه من المسائل المتعلقة بذلك الكتاب، وتمام اسمه مجمع البحرين و ملتقى النهرين . والله أعلم بالصواب.
The author of al-Majma': he is Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Tha'lab Muzaffar al-Din, known as Ibn al-Sa'ati, originally from Baalbek, and raised in Baghdad, died in the year 694 AH. He had a daughter named Fatima. She studied fiqh with her father and took from him Majma' al-Bahrayn, and she used to write good annotations. His father Ali ibn Tha'lab is the one who made the clocks on the Mustansiriyya gate in Baghdad, and was famous in astronomy and astrology, and clock-making. Al-Majma' is a book in which he collected the versified questions of al-Quduri with additions, and he arranged it excellently, and was innovative in its abridgment. At the end of each book, he mentions the difficult questions related to that book. Its full name is Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This entry covers Ibn al-Sa'ati, author of 'Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn', a unique Hanafi fiqh work. The text notes his origins and his father's profession as a clock-maker and astronomer. The work itself is a collection of al-Quduri's versified text (probably al-Quduri's poem on fiqh) with additions, arranged thematically, with a special feature: at the end of each book, he lists difficult issues (mushkilat) related to that book. The entry also mentions his daughter Fatima, who studied and wrote annotations, indicating scholarly activity. This book is a useful reference for a mufti due to its organization and inclusion of problematic issues.

Key Terms
مجمع البحرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn): A Hanafi fiqh work by Ibn al-Sa'ati, compiling al-Quduri's versified text with additions and problematic issues.
ابن الساعاتي (Ibn al-Sa'ati): Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Tha'lab, the author of Majma' al-Bahrayn, died 694 AH.
ما شد منه (ma shadda minhu): The difficult or problematic issues related to a chapter, listed at the end of each book in Majma' al-Bahrayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A list of all the hadiths used
B) A summary of the book's rulings
C) The difficult questions related to that book
D) A biography of the author

Key Takeaway
Majma' al-Bahrayn is a valuable auxiliary work for a mufti because it flags difficult cases systematically, but it must be used alongside primary sources for definitive fatwa.

Biography of al-Mawsili and His Work al-Mukhtar
Biographical entry of al-Mawsili

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of al-Mukhtar, state his full name, his lifespan, and the relationship between al-Mukhtar and al-Ikhtiyar.

Core Idea
Al-Mawsili wrote al-Mukhtar in his youth and later explained it in al-Ikhtiyar.

This lesson introduces a key figure in the Hanafi tradition: Majd al-Din al-Mawsili, author of the foundational text al-Mukhtar. Understanding the author and the textual history helps you assess the authority of his works in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Parse the author's name
The entry begins with 'صاحب المختار', meaning 'the author of al-Mukhtar'. Identify the full name: عبد الله بن محمود بن مودود بن محمود أبو الفضل مجد الدين الموصلى. This reveals his lineage and honorifics.
The title 'مجد الدين' indicates he was a respected scholar.
2
Extract the timeline
Note the birth year (599 AH), that he wrote al-Mukhtar in his youth, later composed its commentary, and died in 683 AH. The commentary was written after the matn.
The phrase 'في عنفوان شبابه' means 'in the prime of his youth'.
3
Understand the textual relationship
Al-Ikhtiyar is a commentary (sharh) on al-Mukhtar. The instruction 'راجع: الاختيار' directs readers to the commentary for more detail. This shows that al-Mawsili himself expanded his own matn.
Al-Mukhtar and al-Ikhtiyar are both standard Hanafi references.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب المختار : هو عبد الله بن محمود بن مودود بن محمود أبو الفضل مجد الدين الموصلى . ولد بالموصل سنة ٥٩٩هـ . وألف "المختار " في عنفوان شبابه، ثم صنف شرحاله ، وسماه بـ "الاختيار" ، مات يوم السبت التاسع عشر من المحرم سنة ٦٨٣هـ . راجع : الاختيار .

This entry covers al-Mawsili, the author of 'al-Mukhtar', which is a well-known Hanafi fiqh text. The death date is given precisely. Both al-Mukhtar and its commentary al-Ikhtiyar are widely used in Hanafi madrasas and are considered reliable texts. The instruction 'Raji': al-Ikhtiyar' likely directs the reader to the commentary for more detail.

Key Terms

Identifying the Author of al-Wiqayah: Lineage and Clarification
Biographical entry clarifying authorship and lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name and lineage of the author of al-Wiqayah and resolve the common confusion between him and his grandson the commentator.

Core Idea
Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud wrote al-Wiqayah; his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah wrote its famous commentary.

This lesson delves into the biography of the venerable Hanafi jurist Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, author of the widely studied matn al-Wiqayah. We will clarify his family lineage, the relationship to the commentator, and address a famous confusion that appears in some secondary sources. Understanding this chain is essential for a mufti to properly attribute rulings and appreciate the transmission of knowledge in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author's Full Name
From the source text, extract the complete name of the author of al-Wiqayah, including his titles and lineage: 'Imam Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah Jamal al-Din al-Abbadi al-Mahbubi al-Bukhari'.
Note the multiple honorifics (Taj al-Shari'ah, Sadr al-Shari'ah) that indicate scholarly rank.
2
Understand the Purpose of al-Wiqayah
The text states that al-Wiqayah was compiled as a selection from al-Hidayah for the author's grandson, Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah. This shows the pedagogical intention behind the work.
3
Distinguish Author from Commentator
The author's grandson, Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud, wrote the famous Sharh al-Wiqayah. They are two distinct individuals. The author is the paternal grandfather.
The commentator later abridged his own commentary as al-Niqayah and wrote al-Tanqih and al-Tawdih in usul.
4
Address the Conflicting Report
The text mentions that al-Qahistani and others claimed the author is Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud (brother of Taj al-Shari'ah). However, the majority view, supported by the text's own research, is that the author is Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, the grandfather.
This confusion arises from similar names and titles within the same family of scholars.
5
Map the Scholarly Family Tree
The source provides names of multiple generations: Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar Ahmad (father of Taj al-Shari'ah), Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud (author), his son? (not named), and his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah (commentator). Also mention of Burhan al-Din (maternal grandfather).
Keeping track of these relationships helps in understanding the chain of transmission of Hanafi knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب الوقاية : هو الإمام تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة أحمد ابن عبيد الله جمال الدين العبادي المحبوبي البخاري. أخذ العلم عن أبيه صدر الشريعة الأكبر أحمد عن أبيه ، كان عالماً ،فاضلا ،تحریراً ،كاملا محققا، مدققا . ألف كتاب الوقاية الذي انتخبه من الهداية، صنّفه لأجل ابن ابنه صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود ابن تاج الشريعة، كذا في أعلام الأخيار ، وفيه أيضا : عبيد الله صدر الشريعة ابن مسعود ابن تاج الشريعة صاحب شرح الوقاية، حافظ قوانين الشرع، ملخص الأصل والفرع عالم المعقول والمنقول، فقيه، أصولي، محدث، مفسر، أخذ العلم عن جده تاج الشريعة محمود، وكان ذا عناية بتقييد نفائس جده وجمع فوائده، شرح الوقاية من تصانيف جده تاج الشريعة ثم اختصره وسماه "النقاية . وألف في الأصول متنا سمّاه التنقيح " ثم صنّف شرحا سماه " التوضيح " . مات سنة ٧٤٧هـ، ومرقد والديه وأولاده وأجداد والديه في شرع آباد "بخارى"، وأما جده (أبو أبيه) تاج الشريعة، وأبو والدته برهان الدين، فإنهما ماتا في "الكرمان " ، ودفنا فيه كذا ذكره عبد الباقي الخطيب بالمدينة المنورة. وفى مدينة العلوم : من شروح الهداية نهاية الكفاية" لتاج الشريعة وهو ،محمود كان عالماً، ،فاضلا ،كاملا، وله مختصر الهداية المسمّى بـ" الوقاية " . أقول : هذا كله نص على أن مصنّف الوقاية هو شارح الهداية تاج الشريعة، وإن اسمه محمود ابن صدر الشريعة الأكبر، وإنه جد صدر الشريعة شارح الوقاية من قبل أبيه، والمشهور أن مصنف "الوقاية " جد فاسد لشارح الوقاية، وبه صرح القهستاني في جامع الرموز حيث ذكر : أن شارح الوقاية صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة عمر ابن صدر الشريعة وإن صاحب الوقاية، برهان الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة أخو تاج الشريعة وكذا ذكره صاحب الكشف : "أن الوقاية للإمام برهان الدين
The author of al-Wiqayah: he is Imam Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah Jamal al-Din al-Abbadi al-Mahbubi al-Bukhari. He took knowledge from his father Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar Ahmad from his father. He was a scholar, virtuous, independent, perfect, a verifier, a scrutinizer. He authored the book al-Wiqayah, which he selected from al-Hidayah, and compiled it for his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah. Thus in A'lam al-Akhyar, and in it also: Ubayd Allah Sadr al-Shari'ah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah, author of the commentary on al-Wiqayah, preserver of the laws of Shari'ah, summarizer of the sources and branches, scholar of the rational and transmitted, a faqih, usuli, muhaddith, mufassir. He took knowledge from his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, and he was concerned with recording the treasures of his grandfather and collecting his benefits. He commented on al-Wiqayah from the works of his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah, then abridged it and called it al-Niqayah. He authored in usul a text called al-Tanqih, then composed a commentary called al-Tawdih. He died in 747 AH. The graves of his parents, children, and his parents' ancestors are in Shar'abad, Bukhara. As for his grandfather (father's father) Taj al-Shari'ah, and his maternal grandfather Burhan al-Din, they died in Kirman and were buried there. This was mentioned by Abd al-Baqi al-Khatib in Medina. In Madinat al-Ulum: from the commentaries of al-Hidayah is Nihayat al-Kifayah by Taj al-Shari'ah, and he was Mahmud, a scholar, virtuous, perfect, and he has a mukhtasar of al-Hidayah called al-Wiqayah. I say: All this is a text that the author of al-Wiqayah is the commentator of al-Hidayah Taj al-Shari'ah, and that his name is Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, and that he is the paternal grandfather of Sadr al-Shari'ah the commentator of al-Wiqayah. And the famous thing is that the author of al-Wiqayah is the corrupted grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqayah, and Qahistani stated in Jami' al-Rumuz where he mentioned that the commentator of al-Wiqayah is Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Umar ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah, and that the author of al-Wiqayah is Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah, the brother of Taj al-Shari'ah. And likewise the author of al-Kashf mentioned: 'Al-Wiqayah is by Imam Burhan al-Din'.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This is a detailed biographical entry on the author of al-Wiqayah, a well-known abridgment of al-Hidayah. The entry clarifies the identity and lineage of the scholar. It identifies the author as Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad, who compiled al-Wiqayah for his grandson. However, the text notes a famous confusion: the actual author is Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, the grandfather of the commentator Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah. Some researchers, like Qahistani, claim that the author is Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud, the brother of Taj al-Shari'ah. The entry also provides details about other members of the family, including the commentator who wrote the famous Sharh al-Wiqayah, and his son who authored al-Niqayah. The death places and dates are given. This clarifies the relationship between the two Sadr al-Shari'ahs and Taj al-Shari'ah. This is important for a mufti to know the chain of transmission and authority of al-Wiqayah and its commentary.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A Hanafi fiqh text selected from al-Hidayah by Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, widely used as a matn.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): Title meaning 'Crown of the Shari'ah', referring to the author of al-Wiqayah, Mahmud ibn Ahmad.
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): Title meaning 'Foremost of the Shari'ah', used for multiple scholars in the family, particularly the grandfather Ahmad and the grandson Ubayd Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, for whom did Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud compile al-Wiqayah?
A) For his own teacher
B) For his grandson, Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah
C) For the general public
D) For the caliph of the time

Key Takeaway
The author of al-Wiqayah is unequivocally Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, the grandfather of the commentator Sadr al-Shari'ah, as clarified by multiple sources in the text.
